Sleep and Unconsciousness as Nullifiers of Wudu
Rulings on sleep, unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication, and imbecility as nullifiers of wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which states of unconsciousness nullify wudu and explain the Hanafi position on sleep positions.

Core Idea
Sleep nullifies wudu only in positions that relax the body; unconsciousness and insanity nullify but imbecility does not.

This lesson examines the ruling of sleep, unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication, and imbecility on wudu. The Hanafi school distinguishes between different types of sleep based on the likelihood of gas release, and treats loss of intellect as a nullifier. The key proof is a hadith restricting nullification to sleep while lying down.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List each state: sleep in various positions, unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication, and imbecility. Determine which nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school.
Sleep nullifies only in lying down (muḍṭajiʿ) or sitting with knees up (mutawarrik). Unconsciousness, insanity, and intoxication nullify; imbecility does not.
2
Examine the dalil for sleep
The hadith 'إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعاً' restricts wudu nullification to those who sleep lying down. Understand the reasoning: relaxation of joints leads to likely escape of gas.
The hadith is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Define key terms
Define muḍṭajiʿ (lying on side), mutawarrik (sitting with buttocks on ground), ighmā (unconsciousness), junūn (insanity), sukr (intoxication), and ʿatah (imbecility). Note the distinctions.
Unconsciousness differs from insanity; prophets can experience ighmā but not junūn.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Consider a person sleeping while standing: wudu remains. A person who becomes unconscious due to illness: wudu nullified. An intoxicated person who cannot walk straight: wudu nullified.
The definition of intoxication includes loss of intellect and change in gait.
5
Note the exemption of imbecility
Imbecility (confused speech and poor management but not beating) does not nullify wudu, unlike insanity. Worship performed by an imbecile is valid.
The source from Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونوم مضطجع إلخ شروع في الكلام على الناقض الحكمي بناء على أن عينه ليس بناقض، بل ما لا يخلو عنه النائم، وقيل: عينه ناقض بالسنة المروية فيه، وهو قوله عليه: "إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعاً"، والاضطجاع: وضع الجنب على الأرض، ويلتحق بالمضطجع من كان في معناه من المستلقي والمنكب يعني ينقض الوضوء النوم من المضطجع والمتورك، وهو احتراز عن النوم قائماً أو راكعاً أو ساجداً؛ لأن الاضطجاع والتورك بسبب استرخاء المفاصل قل ما يخلو عن خروج شيء عادة، والثابت عادة كالمتيقن به وكذا الاتكاء يزيل مسكة اليقظة لزوال المقعد عن الأرض، كذا في "الهداية"، وتفسير التورك: أن يخرج أليتيه على الأرض، والنوم: فترة طبيعية تحدث في الإنسان بلا اختيار منه، وتمنع الحواس الظاهرة والباطنة عن العمل مع سلامتها واستعمال العقل مع قيامه، فيعجز العبد عن أداء الحقوق. (فتح، بحر) وإغماء إلخ الإغماء: آفة في القلب أو الدماغ تعطل القوى المدركة والمحركة مع بقاء العقل مغلوباً، والجنون: زوال العقل، وعلى هذا صح الإغماء على الأنبياء الا دون الجنون، ثم ظاهره أن العته غير ناقض وهو اختلاط في الكلام وفساد التدبير إلا أن صاحبه لا يضرب ولا يشتم؛ لحكمهم على العبادة بالصحة مع العته بخلاف المجنون. (فتح) وسكر: هو سكر يغلب على العقل بمباشرة بعض الأسباب الموجبة له، فيمتنع الإنسان عن العمل بموجب عقله يزيله، ولذا بقي أهلاً للخطاب، ثم اعلم أن حد السكران ههنا ما هو حد السكران في باب الحد، الرجل من المرأة، وهذا الحد ليس بلازم، بل إذا دخل في مشيته تحول فهو سكر، ينتقض به وضوؤه. (بحر، مسكين) وقهقهة إلخ : يعني ينقض الوضوء قهقهة مصل، قيد بالقهقهة؛ لأن الضحك لا ينقض الوضوء، بل يفسد الصلاة، والتبسم لا ينقض شيئاً منهما، والقهقهة خارج الصلاة ليست بناقض، وكذا قهقهة الصبي ليس بناقض، والمراد بالمصلي صلاة ذات ركوع وسجود احترازاً عن صلاة الجنازة، وأن يكون المصلي يقظان، فقهقهة النائم لا ينقض وضوءه في الركوع والسجود، والأصل في ذلك أن النص متى ورد مخالف القياس يقتصر على مورد السماع كذا في "أصول البزدوي"، وحد القهقهة: أن يكون مسموعاً لجيرانه، وحد الضحك أن يكون مسموعاً له دون جيرانه.
And sleep lying down etc.: Beginning of speech on the legal nullifier based on the fact that its essence is not a nullifier, but rather what the sleeper is never free from. And it was said: its essence is a nullifier based on the transmitted sunnah in it, which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Wudu is only upon the one who sleeps lying down.' And lying down is placing the side on the ground. And annexed to the one lying down is anyone in his meaning: the one lying on his back and the one on his side. It means that sleep from the one lying down and the one sitting with knees up (mutawarrik) nullifies wudu, and it is a reservation from sleep standing, bowing, or prostrating because lying down and sitting with knees up, due to the relaxation of joints, rarely are free from the exit of something usually, and what is established by habit is like what is certain. And similarly, leaning removes the grip of wakefulness due to the removal of the seat from the ground. So in al-Hidaya. And the explanation of tawarruk: that he puts his buttocks on the ground. And sleep is a natural period that occurs in a person without his choice, and it prevents the apparent and inner senses from working while they are sound, and the use of intellect while it is standing, so the servant becomes incapable of fulfilling rights. (Fath, Bahr) And unconsciousness etc.: Unconsciousness is a malady in the heart or brain that disables the perceptive and motor faculties while the intellect remains overwhelmed. And insanity is the loss of intellect, and accordingly, unconsciousness is possible for prophets, but not insanity. Then it appears that imbecility (atah) is not a nullifier, and it is confusion in speech and corruption of management, but its owner is not beaten or insulted because they judge worship to be valid with imbecility, unlike the insane. (Fath) And intoxication: it is intoxication that overwhelms the intellect by directly engaging in some of its causes, so a person is prevented from acting according to his intellect and removes it, so he remains eligible for address. Then know that the definition of the intoxicated here is the same as the definition of the intoxicated in the chapter of hudud, the man from the woman. And this definition is not necessary, but if he enters his walk and changes, then it is intoxication, and his wudu is nullified by it. (Bahr, Miskin) And laughter etc.: meaning the guffaw of a person in prayer nullifies wudu, restricted to guffaw because laughter does not nullify wudu but rather invalidates prayer, and a smile does not nullify either. And guffaw outside prayer is not a nullifier, and similarly the guffaw of a child is not a nullifier. And by 'person in prayer' is meant prayer with bowing and prostration, as a precaution against funeral prayer. And that the person in prayer is awake, so the guffaw of a sleeping person does not nullify his wudu in bowing and prostration. And the principle in that is that when the text comes contrary to analogy, it is restricted to the scope of the narration. So in Usul al-Bazdawi. And the definition of guffaw: that it is heard by his neighbors, and the definition of laughter: that it is heard by him but not by his neighbors.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage covers nullifiers that relate to loss of consciousness and auditory actions. Sleep nullifies wudu only if it occurs in a lying down or sitting-with-knees-up (mutawarrik) position, because these positions lead to relaxation and the likely escape of something. This is based on a hadith that restricts wudu to those who sleep lying down. Unconsciousness (ighma'), insanity (junun), and intoxication (sukr) nullify wudu because they remove intellect or overwhelm it; however, imbecility (atah) does not nullify. Laughter (qahqaha) during prayer nullifies wudu, but only if it is loud (audible to neighbors) and during a prayer that has bowing and prostration. Smiling and ordinary laughter do not nullify wudu (though laughter invalidates prayer). The passage also emphasizes that these rulings are based on transmitted texts that may be contrary to analogy, so they are applied strictly.

Key Terms
نوم مضطجع (nawm muḍṭaji‘): Sleep while lying on one's side.
إغماء (ighmā): Unconsciousness due to a malady in heart or brain; intellect is overwhelmed.
جنون (junūn): Loss of intellect.
سكر (sukr): Intoxication that overwhelms the intellect.
عته (atah): Imbecility; confusion in speech and poor management, but intellect not lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sleep while lying on your back
B) Unconsciousness due to fainting
C) Imbecility (confusion in speech)
D) Intoxication leading to unsteady walk

Key Takeaway
Sleep nullifies wudu only when in a position of full relaxation; unconsciousness and intoxication nullify due to loss of intellect; imbecility does not nullify.

Laughter as a Nullifier of Wudu in Prayer
Ruling on loud laughter during prayer as a nullifier of wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between loud laughter, ordinary laughter, and smile in terms of their effect on wudu and prayer validity.

Core Idea
Only loud laughter (qahqaha) during a valid prayer with bowing and prostration nullifies wudu.

This lesson focuses on the specific ruling regarding laughter during prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between qahqaha (loud laughter), dahiik (ordinary laughter), and tabassum (smile). The passage explains that only qahqaha while in a prayer that includes ruku and sujud nullifies wudu, based on a principle that texts contrary to analogy are applied restrictively.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate types of laughter
Define qahqaha (audible to neighbors), dahiik (audible to the person only), and tabassum (no sound). Note their rulings.
Qahqaha nullifies wudu and invalidates prayer; dahiik invalidates prayer only; tabassum does nothing.
2
Identify conditions for nullification
Nullification occurs only when qahqaha happens during a prayer that includes ruku and sujud (not funeral prayer), and the person is awake.
Qahqaha outside prayer does not nullify wudu.
3
Understand the textual basis
The passage cites the principle from Usul al-Bazdawi: 'When a text comes contrary to analogy, it is restricted to the scope of the narration.' The hadith or report about laughter nullifying wudu is applied narrowly.
This principle limits the ruling to the exact scenario reported.
4
Apply to scenarios
A person laughs loudly during fajr prayer so that neighbors can hear: wudu nullified. A person chuckles softly during prayer: prayer invalid but wudu remains. A person smiles: nothing happens.
The prayer must be one with ruku and sujud; funeral prayer (janaza) is excluded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونوم مضطجع إلخ شروع في الكلام على الناقض الحكمي بناء على أن عينه ليس بناقض، بل ما لا يخلو عنه النائم، وقيل: عينه ناقض بالسنة المروية فيه، وهو قوله عليه: "إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعاً"، والاضطجاع: وضع الجنب على الأرض، ويلتحق بالمضطجع من كان في معناه من المستلقي والمنكب يعني ينقض الوضوء النوم من المضطجع والمتورك، وهو احتراز عن النوم قائماً أو راكعاً أو ساجداً؛ لأن الاضطجاع والتورك بسبب استرخاء المفاصل قل ما يخلو عن خروج شيء عادة، والثابت عادة كالمتيقن به وكذا الاتكاء يزيل مسكة اليقظة لزوال المقعد عن الأرض، كذا في "الهداية"، وتفسير التورك: أن يخرج أليتيه على الأرض، والنوم: فترة طبيعية تحدث في الإنسان بلا اختيار منه، وتمنع الحواس الظاهرة والباطنة عن العمل مع سلامتها واستعمال العقل مع قيامه، فيعجز العبد عن أداء الحقوق. (فتح، بحر) وإغماء إلخ الإغماء: آفة في القلب أو الدماغ تعطل القوى المدركة والمحركة مع بقاء العقل مغلوباً، والجنون: زوال العقل، وعلى هذا صح الإغماء على الأنبياء الا دون الجنون، ثم ظاهره أن العته غير ناقض وهو اختلاط في الكلام وفساد التدبير إلا أن صاحبه لا يضرب ولا يشتم؛ لحكمهم على العبادة بالصحة مع العته بخلاف المجنون. (فتح) وسكر: هو سكر يغلب على العقل بمباشرة بعض الأسباب الموجبة له، فيمتنع الإنسان عن العمل بموجب عقله يزيله، ولذا بقي أهلاً للخطاب، ثم اعلم أن حد السكران ههنا ما هو حد السكران في باب الحد، الرجل من المرأة، وهذا الحد ليس بلازم، بل إذا دخل في مشيته تحول فهو سكر، ينتقض به وضوؤه. (بحر، مسكين) وقهقهة إلخ : يعني ينقض الوضوء قهقهة مصل، قيد بالقهقهة؛ لأن الضحك لا ينقض الوضوء، بل يفسد الصلاة، والتبسم لا ينقض شيئاً منهما، والقهقهة خارج الصلاة ليست بناقض، وكذا قهقهة الصبي ليس بناقض، والمراد بالمصلي صلاة ذات ركوع وسجود احترازاً عن صلاة الجنازة، وأن يكون المصلي يقظان، فقهقهة النائم لا ينقض وضوءه في الركوع والسجود، والأصل في ذلك أن النص متى ورد مخالف القياس يقتصر على مورد السماع كذا في "أصول البزدوي"، وحد القهقهة: أن يكون مسموعاً لجيرانه، وحد الضحك أن يكون مسموعاً له دون جيرانه.
And sleep lying down etc.: Beginning of speech on the legal nullifier based on the fact that its essence is not a nullifier, but rather what the sleeper is never free from. Nullification by Vomiting: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Scattered Vomit
Intra-Hanafi dispute on collecting scattered vomit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on collecting scattered vomit and identify the conditions under which it is collected according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and determine which view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Scattered vomit is collected only if the cause (nausea) is unified; sitting alone is insufficient.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nullification of wudu by vomiting. When vomit occurs in multiple instances, should they be combined to determine if a mouthful is reached? The Hanafi school has two opinions: Abu Yusuf uses the unity of the sitting, while Muhammad uses the unity of the cause (nausea). The relied-upon view is Muhammad's.

Guided Path
1
Understand the baseline ruling
Recall that in the Hanafi school, vomiting a mouthful nullifies wudu. The issue here is when vomit occurs in scattered instances.
A mouthful is defined as vomit that fills the mouth.
2
Identify the two opinions
Abu Yusuf holds that scattered vomit is collected if the sitting (majlis) is the same, regardless of the cause. Muhammad holds that it is collected only if the cause (nausea) is the same.
Both are valid positions within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the four scenarios
The passage outlines four scenarios based on unity of sitting and cause: both unified (collected by agreement), both different (not collected by agreement), sitting unified alone (collected per Abu Yusuf), cause unified alone (collected per Muhammad).
The reliance on each scenario determines the ruling.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'al-ashah qawl Muhammad' (the more correct is the saying of Muhammad). Therefore, the operative ruling is that the cause (nausea) must be unified for collection.
This is the view adopted for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متفرقه: أي متفرق القيء، يعني إذا كان القيء متفرقاً، ولو جمع يصير ملء الفم يجمع إن اتحد السبب وهو الغثيان مثلاً، فإن قاء ثانياً وثالثاً قبل سكون النفس من الغثيان الأول كان السبب متحداً فيجمع، وإن قاء بعده وكان الغثيان مختلفاً فلا يجمع، وقال أبو يوسف يجمع إن اتحد المجلس، سواء كان السبب مختلفاً أو لا، والأصح قول محمد. (مسكين) وهو على أربعة أوجه إما أن يكون المجلس والسبب متحدين فيجمع ا اتفاقاً، وإما متعددين اتفاقاً، يجمع وإما أن يكون المجلس متحداً لا غير، فيجمع عند أبي يوسف وإما أن يكون الغثيان متحداً لا غير، فعند محمد يجمع. [رمز الحقائق: ١٥/١]
Vomit that is scattered: meaning scattered vomit, meaning if the vomit is scattered, and if collected it would fill the mouth, it is collected if the cause is unified, such as nausea. If he vomits a second and third time before the calm of the breath from the first nausea, the cause is unified, so it is collected. If he vomits after that and the nausea is different, it is not collected. Abu Yusuf said: it is collected if the sitting is unified, whether the cause is different or not. The more correct is the saying of Muhammad. (Miskin) It has four aspects: either the sitting and cause are unified, so it is collected by agreement; or both are multiple, by agreement it is not collected; or the sitting is unified only, then according to Abu Yusuf it is collected; or the nausea is unified only, then according to Muhammad it is collected. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 15/1]
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage discusses the nullification of wudu by vomiting, specifically when vomit occurs in multiple instances. The issue is whether the vomit should be collected to determine if it reaches a mouthful. The Hanafi school generally holds that vomiting a mouthful nullifies wudu. Here, the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the condition for collecting scattered vomit: it depends on the unity of the cause (nausea) and the unity of the sitting (majlis). Abu Yusuf considers the sitting alone sufficient for collection, while Muhammad considers the cause alone sufficient. The relied-upon view is Muhammad's, as indicated by 'al-ashah' (more correct). The passage then outlines four possible scenarios and the respective rulings by agreement or disagreement.

Key Terms
متفرقه (mutafarriqah): Scattered vomit – vomit occurring in multiple instances rather than one continuous discharge.
قيء (qay'): Vomit – the matter ejected from the stomach through the mouth.
غثيان (ghathayan): Nausea – the urge to vomit; considered the cause (sabab) of vomiting.
مجلس (majlis): Sitting – the physical sitting session or place where the person remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if the sitting (majlis) is the same, regardless of the cause.
B) Only if the cause (ghathayan) is the same, regardless of the sitting.
C) Neither; each instance is considered separately.
D) Only if both the sitting and cause are the same.

Key Takeaway
Scattered vomit is collected for wudu nullification only if the cause (nausea) is unified; the unity of sitting alone is insufficient per the relied-upon view.

Qahqaha: Does Loud Laughter Nullify Wudu During Prayer?
Inter-madhhab dispute on qahqaha nullifying wuḍūʾ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qahqaha, dahik, and tabassum regarding their effects on wudu and prayer, and explain why the Hanafi school gives priority to the hadith over qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Loud laughter in prayer nullifies wudu; the text overrides analogy.

This passage from a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the precise ruling on laughter during prayer. While many assume any laughter breaks wudu, the Hanafi school distinguishes three levels of laughter with different effects. The passage also presents the Shafi'i counter‑argument based on analogy and the Hanafi response grounded in a specific hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of laughter
Distinguish qahqaha (audible to neighbours), dahik (audible only to oneself), and tabassum (no sound). Note who defines them and their legal effects.
The source gives clear acoustic boundaries.
2
State the Hanafi position
Qahqaha during a prayer with rukūʿ and sujūd nullifies wuḍūʾ and invalidates the prayer. Outside prayer and for children it has no effect.
The ruling is limited to prayers that include bowing and prostration.
3
Examine the Shāfiʿī objection
The Shāfiʿī school argues by qiyās: laughter is not an impure emission, so it cannot be a ḥadath. Therefore it should not nullify wuḍūʾ.
This is the counter‑analogy presented in the text.
4
Analyse the Ḥanafī proof
The Ḥanafīs rely on the ḥadīth of the blind man: the Prophet ﷺ ordered the laugher to repeat both wuḍūʾ and prayer. Because a text (naṣṣ) contradicts qiyās, the text prevails and the ruling is restricted to the reported case.
From Uṣūl al‑Bazdawī: ‘When a text comes contrary to analogy, it is restricted to the reported case.’
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarat al‑khilāf)
If a person laughs aloud in a regular prayer: Ḥanafī – must repeat wuḍūʾ and prayer; Shāfiʿī – wuḍūʾ remains valid, prayer may need repetition if the laughter was intentional.
This difference affects how a person acts after such an incident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقهقهة إلخ : يعني ينقض الوضوء قهقهة مصل، قيد بالقهقهة؛ لأن الضحك لا ينقض الوضوء، بل يفسد الصلاة، والتبسم لا ينقض شيئاً منهما، والقهقهة خارج الصلاة ليست بناقض، وكذا قهقهة الصبي ليس بناقض، والمراد بالمصلي صلاة ذات ركوع وسجود احترازاً عن صلاة الجنازة، وأن يكون المصلي يقظان، فقهقهة النائم لا ينقض وضوءه في الركوع والسجود، والأصل في ذلك أن النص متى ورد مخالف القياس يقتصر على مورد السماع كذا في "أصول البزدوي"، وحد القهقهة: أن يكون مسموعاً لجيرانه، وحد الضحك أن يكون مسموعاً له دون جيرانه، وحد التبسم: أن لا يكون مسموعا له ولا لجيرانه، وكون القهقهة ناقضاً هو مذهبنا، وقال الشافعي: لا ينقض، وهو القياس؛ لأنه ليس بخارج نجساً، ولهذا لم يكن حدثاً في خارج الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة، ولنا ما روي أن أعمى تردى في بئر والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي بأصحابه، فضحك بعض من كان معه، فأمره أن يعيد الوضوء والصلاة، فالقياس بمقابلة هذا النص مردود. (فتح، مسكين وغيره)
And qahqaha etc.: meaning that laughing aloud (qahqaha) of a praying person nullifies wudu. It is restricted to qahqaha because ordinary laughter (dahik) does not nullify wudu but invalidates the prayer, and smiling (tabassum) does not nullify either. Qahqaha outside prayer is not a nullifier, and likewise the qahqaha of a child is not a nullifier. By 'praying person' is meant one performing a prayer that has bowing and prostration, to exclude the funeral prayer, and that the person is awake, so the qahqaha of a sleeping person does not nullify wudu. The principle is that when a text comes contrary to analogy, it is restricted to the case reported. The definition of qahqaha: it is audible to one's neighbors; dahik: audible to oneself but not to neighbors; tabassum: not audible to oneself nor to neighbors. That qahqaha is a nullifier is our school. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not nullify, and that is the analogy because it is not an impure emission, hence it is not a hadath outside prayer nor in prostration of recitation. Our proof is the report that a blind man fell into a well while the Prophet was praying with his companions, and one of them laughed, so he ordered him to repeat the wudu and prayer. Analogy in the face of this text is rejected.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the ruling that laughing aloud (qahqaha) during prayer nullifies wudu. The author distinguishes between qahqaha (heard by others), dahik (heard only by oneself), and tabassum (not heard). Only qahqaha nullifies wudu and only during a prayer that includes bowing and prostration. The Shafi'i school opposes, arguing by analogy that since laughter is not an impure substance, it should not be a hadath. The Hanafi school responds with a hadith: a companion laughed when a blind man fell, and the Prophet ordered him to repeat wudu and prayer. The principle stated is that when a text contradicts analogy, the text takes precedence, and the ruling is limited to the specific case mentioned.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter audible to neighbors; the only type of laughter that nullifies wudu during prayer.
ضحك (dahik): Ordinary laughter audible only to oneself; does not nullify wudu but invalidates prayer.
تبسم (tabassum): Smiling without sound; does not nullify wudu nor invalidate prayer.
نقض (naqd): Nullification – the act of breaking wudu; a hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person laughs aloud (qahqaha) during the funeral prayer (ṣalāt al‑janāzah)?
A) It nullifies wuḍūʾ and invalidates the prayer.
B) It nullifies wuḍūʾ but does not invalidate the prayer.
C) It does not nullify wuḍūʾ but invalidates the prayer.
D) It does not nullify wuḍūʾ nor invalidate the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Qahqaha during a prayer with rukūʿ and sujūd nullifies wuḍūʾ and invalidates the prayer, based on a ḥadīth that overrides qiyās.

Obligatory Acts of Ghusl: Mouth and Nose
Inter-madhhab dispute on rinsing mouth and nose in ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rinsing the mouth and nose in ghusl, cite the Quranic proof, and distinguish the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Rinsing the mouth and nose is fard in ghusl because the Quran commands complete purification of all washable parts.

This passage addresses a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq) are obligatory or sunnah in ghusl. You will learn the Hanafi proof from the Quran and how it differs from the case of wudu, where these acts are sunnah. Understanding this distinction ensures your ghusl is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the text declares as fard in ghusl: washing the mouth and nose. Confirm the Hanafi ruling that these are obligatory.
The text opens by stating the fara'id of ghusl.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
The text mentions al-Shafi'i, who holds these acts are sunnah based on the hadith of fitrah. Note the specific acts listed in the hadith, including madmadah and istinshaq.
The Shafi'i argument relies on this hadith and analogy with wudu.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response cites the Quranic verse 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves.' The argument is that every washable part must be purified, and the mouth and nose are washable internally.
The key distinction: in wudu, the face is defined externally, so interior is not required; in ghusl, the entire body is required.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one omits madmadah or istinshaq, the Hanafi say ghusl is invalid; the Shafi'i say it is valid but recommended to perform them.
This affects daily practice: a Hanafi must redo ghusl if these are missed.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text clearly sides with the Hanafi view. In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi is that these are fard. Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf (difference of opinion).
The Quranic evidence is considered stronger in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرائض الغسل] وفرض الغسل: غسل فمه وأنفه . أي المضمضة أي الاستنشاق، وقال الشافعي: إنهما سنتان؛ لقوله عليه: "عشرة من الفطرة"، أي السنة وهي قص الشارب وإعفاء اللحية والسواك والمضمضة والاستنشاق وقص الأظفار وغسل البراجم ونتف الإبط وحلق العانة وانتقاص الماء، ولهذا كانا سنتين في الوضوء، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ كُنْتُمْ جُنُباً فَاطَهَّرُوا (المائدة: ٦)، فكل ما أمكن تطهيره يجب غسله، وباطن الفم والأنف يمكن غسله، بخلاف الوضوء؛ لأنه يجب فيه غسل الوجه، وهو ما تقع به المواجهة، ولا تقع المواجهة بداخل الفم والأنف. (فتح)
The obligatory acts of ghusl: And the fard of ghusl is washing his mouth and his nose i.e. rinsing (madmadah) and snuffing (istinshaq). Al-Shafi'i said: they are sunnah based on his saying: 'Ten are from fitrah' meaning sunnah: trimming the mustache, letting the beard grow, siwak, rinsing the mouth, snuffing water, clipping nails, washing knuckles, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, and using water sparingly. Hence these are sunnah in wudu. Our proof is His saying: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (al-Ma'idah: 6). Everything that can be purified must be washed, and the interior of the mouth and nose can be washed. This differs from wudu because in wudu the face must be washed, which is what is faced, and the interior of the mouth and nose are not faced.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligatory acts (fara'id) of ghusl. The Hanafi school holds that rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and snuffing water into the nose (istinshaq) are fard (obligatory) in ghusl. The Shafi'i school considers them sunnah based on a hadith listing practices of fitrah, where these acts are mentioned alongside other sunan. The Hanafi response uses the Quranic verse (5:6) which commands purification when in a state of janabah. They argue that since the interior of the mouth and nose can be washed and purification requires washing everything washable, these parts must be washed. In contrast, in wudu, the face is defined as the exterior part that is faced; thus the interior of the mouth and nose are not part of the face, so they are sunnah in wudu but fard in ghusl.

Key Terms
فرائض الغسل (fara'id al-ghusl): The obligatory components of ghusl (ritual bath); washing the entire body, including mouth and nose.
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Snuffing water into the nose and then expelling it.
فطرة (fitrah): The natural state or practices of the prophets; acts considered sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of rinsing the mouth (madmadah) in ghusl?
A) Fard (obligatory), and omitting it invalidates ghusl.
B) Sunnah muakkadah, and omitting it is makruh but ghusl is valid.
C) Sunnah ghayr muakkadah, and omitting it is permissible.
D) Mubah, neither required nor recommended.

Key Takeaway
Rinsing the mouth and nose are obligatory (fard) in ghusl according to the Hanafi school, based on the Quranic command for complete purification.

Fard Acts of Ghusl: Madmadah and Istinshaq (Hanafi vs Shafi'i)
Establishing that rinsing mouth and nose are fard in ghusl with dalil from Quran, and refuting Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on rinsing the mouth and nose in ghusl, explain the Quranic proof, and contrast it with the Shafi'i proof from the fitrah hadith.

Core Idea
In ghusl, the Quran commands purifying every washable part, including the interior of the mouth and nose.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the mandatory acts of ghusl (full ritual bath). While both agree on washing the entire body, they differ on whether rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and nose (istinshaq) are obligatory (fard) or merely sunnah. The Hanafi school, relying on the general command of Quran 5:6, holds that these are fard. The Shafi'i school cites a hadith listing them among the ten fitrah practices to argue they are sunnah. We will unpack the reasoning of each side and understand the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify what exactly is contested: Are madmadah and istinshaq in ghusl fard or sunnah?
This is an inter-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Locate the Quranic verse cited (5:6) and understand how it is used: 'fa-ttahharu' is a general command to purify all accessible parts.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
3
Identify the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith of the ten fitrah practices, which includes madmadah and istinshaq, implying they are sunnah.
Fitrah practices are considered sunnah, not obligatory.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between wudu and ghusl: in wudu the face is defined externally only, whereas in ghusl the command is broader. The fitrah hadith does not override the Quranic command.
Note the role of Quranic primacy in Hanafi methodology.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis must rinse mouth and nose in ghusl; omission invalidates ghusl. Shafi'is may omit them without invalidation.
This difference affects the validity of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرض الغسل: يجوز أن يكون عطفا على جملة "فرض الوضوء" أو استئنافاً، والغسل بالضم اسم لغسل سائر الجسد، قال في "المغرب": الغسل بالضم اسم من الاغتسال وأراد بالفرض ما يعمّ العملي، فإنه اسم لما يفوت الجواز بفوته أو بمعنى المفروض . (ش) غسل فمه وأنفه وقال الشافعي: إنهما سنتان؛ لقوله عليه: "عشرة من الفطرة"، أي السنة وهي قص الشارب وإعفاء اللحية والسواك والمضمضة والاستنشاق وقص الأظفار وغسل البراجم ونتف الإبط وحلق العانة وانتقاص الماء، ولهذا كانا سنتين في الوضوء، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ كُنتُمْ جُنُباً فَاطَهَّرُوا﴾ (المائدة: ٦)، فكل ما أمكن تطهيره يجب غسله، وباطن الفم والأنف يمكن غسله، بخلاف الوضوء؛ لأنه يجب فيه غسل الوجه، وهو ما تقع به المواجهة، ولا تقع المواجهة بداخل الفم والأنف. (فتح)
And the fard of ghusl: It is permissible that it be a conjunction to the sentence 'the fard of wudu' or an independent statement. Ghusl (with a damma) is a noun meaning the washing of the entire body. He said in al-Mughrib: Ghusl (with a damma) is a noun derived from al-ightsil (bathing). He intended by 'fard' what includes the practical, for it is a name for what causes permissibility to be lost by its loss, or meaning 'that which is made obligatory'. (Sh) Washing of his mouth and his nose. And al-Shafi'i said they are two sunnahs; due to his statement 'Ten things are from fitrah', meaning the sunnah: trimming the moustache, letting the beard grow, siwak, rinsing the mouth, rinsing the nose, trimming nails, washing knuckles, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, and reducing water. For this reason they were two sunnahs in wudu. And for us is His statement 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' (5:6), so everything that can be purified must be washed, and the interior of the mouth and nose can be washed, unlike wudu; because in wudu the face must be washed, which is that with which facing (others) occurs, and facing does not occur inside the mouth and nose. (Fath)
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the fard (obligatory) acts of ghusl (full ritual bath). The author clarifies that 'fard' here means what is necessary for validity—if omitted, the ghusl is invalid. He states that rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and nose (istinshaq) are fard in ghusl. He then reports that Imam al-Shafi'i considers them merely sunnah, based on a hadith listing them among 'ten things from fitrah' (innate practices), implying they are sunnah. The Hanafi response: the Quranic command 'purify yourselves' (5:6) is general; any part of the body that can be purified must be washed. The interior of the mouth and nose are accessible to water, so they must be washed. The distinction from wudu is that in wudu, only the face (what is exposed when facing someone) is required, excluding the mouth and nose interiors. Thus, the Hanafi position is that these rinsings are fard in ghusl due to the broader command.

Key Terms
الغسل بالضم (al-ghusl bi al-damm): The noun form meaning the ritual bath itself.
المضمضة والاستنشاق (al-madmadah wa al-istinshāq): Rinsing the mouth with water (madmadah) and drawing water into the nostrils (istinshaq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider rinsing the mouth and nose obligatory (fard) in ghusl but not in wudu?
A) Because the Quranic command 'purify yourselves' is limited to the external body.
B) Because the mouth and nose are part of the 'face' in wudu.
C) Because the interior of the mouth and nose can be washed and the Quran commands purification of the entire body in ghusl.
D) Because the Prophet always did them in ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Rinsing the mouth and nose are fard in ghusl because the Quranic command to purify includes all accessible interior parts, unlike wudu where only the external face is required.

Sunnah Acts of Ghusl and the Dispute on Rubbing and Foreskin
Listing sunnah acts and debating rubbing and foreskin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of ghusl and explain why rubbing (dalk) is not fard in the Hanafi school, and state the preferred view on washing under the foreskin for an uncircumcised man.

Core Idea
Rubbing is not required because water purifies by contact; the foreskin is treated as internal in ghusl for ease.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the sunnah (recommended) acts of ghusl and addresses two points of legal dispute: whether rubbing the body (dalk) is obligatory and whether water must reach under the foreskin of an uncircumcised man. You will learn the Hanafi position and the reasoning behind it, including the intra-madhhab difference on the foreskin issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts of ghusl
Read the sunnah acts listed: washing hands, private parts, impurities, performing wudu, pouring water three times.
Note that these are recommended, not obligatory.
2
Analyze the dispute on rubbing (dalk)
The text states that rubbing is not fard in the Hanafi school. Compare with the Maliki view and the analogy to washing a garment.
The Hanafi proof is Quran 25:48—water is inherently purifying.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the foreskin
Some mashayikh consider the foreskin as external (requiring water); others as internal (not requiring). The author chooses the latter for ghusl due to hardship.
In wudu, the foreskin is considered external for precaution.
4
Understand the basis for the preferred view
The author's choice balances hardship in ghusl (no requirement) and precaution in wudu (requirement).
This is a practical application of easing difficulty (raf‘ al-haraj).
5
Apply the ruling
State the mufta bihi: dalk is not fard; washing under foreskin is not required in ghusl but is required in wudu.
This affects daily practice for uncircumcised men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الغسل
وبدنه لا دلكه وإدخال الماء داخل الجلد للأقلف.
أي لا يجب أي البدن
[سنن الغسل]
وسنته: أن يغسل يديه وفرجه ونجاسة لو كانت على بدنه، ثم يتوضأ ثم يُفيضُ الماء على بدنه ثلاثاً، ابتداء إلى رسغيه لئلا تشيع. وبطنه [ أي وغسل بدنه ما يمكن فيغسل السرّة وبشرة اللحية ولو كثة، لو عبر بالجسد لكان أولى؛ لأن الأطراف داخلة في الجسد خارجة عن البدن؛ لأن البدن كما في "الدر"- من المنكب إلى الألية، والحاصل أنه يجب غسل ما يكون من ظاهر البدن ولو من وجه كالشارب والحاجب وجميع اللحية؛ إذ لا حرج فيه، وكذا الفرج الخارج لا ما فيه حرج بأن يتعسر إيصال الماء إليه أو يضر، كداخل العينين وباطن الجرح. (فتح) لا دلكه أي دلك البدن في الغسل ليس بفرض عندنا، وقال مالك: هو فرض؛ اعتباراً بغسل الثوب ولأن الغسل هو الفعل، ولا يكون إلا بالدلك، ولنا: أن الماء مطهر بطبعه؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَنْزَلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً طَهُورا ﴾ (الفرقان:٤٨)، فإذا لاقى المحل النجس طهره، بخلاف الثوب؛ لأن النجاسة تخللت في أثنائه. (مستخلص) وإدخال الماء: عطف على قوله : لا دلكه، والأقلف هو الأغلف الذي لم يختن وفي وجوب إدخال الماء داخل الجلدة اختلاف المشايخ، فعند بعضهم لها حكم الظاهر من كل وجه حتى يجب إيصال الماء إليها، وإذا نزل البول ولم يخرج عنها نقض الوضوء، وعند البعض لها حكم الباطن في الغسل حتى لا يجب إيصال الماء إليها ينقض الوضوء بنزول البول إليها، فلها حكم الباطن في الغسل وحكم الظاهر في الوضوء عندهم، واختار المصنف هذا لمكان الحرج في الغسل وللاحتياط في الوضوء. (مستخلص) وسنته إلخ أي سنة الغسل أفاد في البحر": أن ما كان سنة في الوضوء فهو سنة في الغسل، فتسن فيه النية، ويندب التلفظ بها، وكذا يندب فيه ما هو مندوب في الوضوء سوى استقبال القبلة، فإنه يكون غالبا مع العورة وغسل اليدين؛ لأنهما آلة التطهير، ولقوله عليه: "فلا يغمسن يده في الإناء"، أما في غسل الفرج؛ فلأنه لا يخلو حال الجنابة عن النجاسة، وأما غسل النجاسة؛ لئلا تزداد بإصابة الماء. [كشف الحقائق: ١٢/١] فرجه وإن لم يكن به نجاسة. (ط) ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصلاة إلا رجليه إن كانا في مجمع الماء. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧/١] ثم يفيض الماء: أي المعهود في الشرع للغسل والوضوء، وهو ثمانية أرطال، وكيفية الإفاضة أن يبدأ بمنكبه الأيمن، فيفيض الماء عليه ثلاثاً، ثم بمنكبه الأيسر كذلك، ثم يفيض الماء على رأسه وسائر جسده كذلك. (مسكين وغيره) على بدنه [ أي يصب الماء على سائر أعضائه ثلاثاً، هكذا حكت أم المؤمنين ميمونة من غسل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. (مستخلص)] مع أنه كشف
Sunnah acts of ghusl. And his body—no rubbing of it and insertion of water under the foreskin for the uncircumcised. Meaning: it is not obligatory, i.e., the body. [Sunnah of ghusl]: Its sunnah is that he washes his hands, his private parts, and any impurity if on his body, then performs wudu, then pours water over his body three times, beginning up to his wrists to avoid spread. And his belly [i.e., he washes what is possible of his body: he washes the navel and the skin of the beard even if thick; if he said 'body' (jasad) it would be better because the limbs are included in the body (jasad) but outside 'badan'; because badan, as in al-Durr, is from shoulder to buttocks. The conclusion: it is obligatory to wash what is from the apparent parts of the body (badan), even from the face like mustache, eyebrow, and all of the beard, since there is no hardship; likewise the external private parts, not what involves hardship like water reaching difficult or harmful areas such as inside the eyes or the interior of a wound. (Fath) 'No rubbing' means rubbing the body in ghusl is not obligatory in our school, and Malik said it is obligatory; by analogy to washing a garment and because ghusl is an action that cannot be without rubbing. And for us: water is purifying by its nature; due to His statement 'And We sent down from the sky purifying water' (25:48), so when it meets an impure place it purifies it, unlike a garment because the impurity permeates its fibers. (Mukhtasar) 'And insertion of water': conjunction to his statement 'no rubbing', and al-aqlaf is the uncircumcised who has not been circumcised. Regarding the obligation of inserting water under the foreskin, there is a disagreement among the shaykhs: according to some, it has the ruling of the external in every respect, so water must reach it; if urine descends and does not exit from it, it nullifies wudu. According to others, it has the ruling of the internal in ghusl, so water need not reach it; but urine descending to it would nullify wudu. Thus, according to them, it has the ruling of internal for ghusl and external for wudu. The author chose this due to hardship in ghusl and precaution in wudu. (Mukhtasar) 'And its sunnah etc.' means the sunnah of ghusl. It is stated in al-Bahr: what is sunnah in wudu is sunnah in ghusl, so intention (niyyah) is sunnah in it, and verbal expression is recommended, and likewise what is recommended in wudu except facing the qiblah, because that is usually with the 'awrah. And washing hands because they are the tool of purification, due to his statement: 'Let him not dip his hand into the vessel.' As for washing the private part, because the state of janabah is not free from impurity. And as for washing the impurity, so that it does not increase by the water reaching it. [Kashf al-Haqa'iq 12:1] His private part even if no impurity is on it. (T) Then he performs wudu like his wudu for prayer except his feet if they are in the collection of water. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 17:1] Then he pours water: meaning the usual amount in sharia for ghusl and wudu, which is eight ratls. The method of pouring: he starts with his right shoulder, pouring water over it three times, then his left shoulder likewise, then pours water over his head and the rest of his body likewise. (Miskin etc.) Over his body [i.e., he pours water over all his limbs three times. This is how Umm al-Mu'minin Maymunah narrated the ghusl of the Messenger of Allah. (Mukhtasar)] although he unveiled.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq enumerates the sunnah (recommended) acts of ghusl (full bath) and addresses two disputed points: rubbing (dalk) and washing under the foreskin (for an uncircumcised man). The author first states the sunnah acts: washing hands and private parts, cleansing any impurity, performing wudu (except feet if standing in water), then pouring water over the body three times. He notes that the body (badan) must be washed, including the navel, beard, eyebrows, mustache, but not areas of hardship like inside eyes or wounds. Then the text clarifies that rubbing the body is not obligatory (fard) in the Hanafi school, but Imam Malik considers it fard by analogy to washing a garment. The Hanafi response: water is inherently purifying (Quran 25:48); it cleans upon contact, unlike a garment where rubbing is needed due to permeation. Regarding the foreskin: for an uncircumcised man, there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars whether water must reach under the foreskin. Some say it has the ruling of external skin, so water must reach it and urine trapped under it would nullify wudu. Others say it has the ruling of internal skin for ghusl (so not required) but external for wudu (so trapped urine nullifies). The author (likely al-Marghinani) chooses the latter: internal for ghusl due to hardship, external for wudu as a precaution. The passage concludes with the sunnah of pouring water three times, as narrated from the Prophet.

Key Terms
الدلك (al-dalk): Rubbing the body during ghusl to ensure water reaches the skin.
الأقلف (al-aqlaf): An uncircumcised male; refers to the foreskin covering the glans.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, what is the ruling for an uncircumcised man regarding washing under the foreskin in ghusl?
A) It is obligatory (fard) to insert water under the foreskin.
B) It is not obligatory due to hardship, but it is obligatory in wudu.
C) It is a sunnah act.
D) It is forbidden to insert water if it causes pain.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, rubbing is not fard in ghusl, and the foreskin is treated as internal in ghusl but external in wudu, balancing ease and precaution.

The Fard of Washing the Body and the Non-Fard of Rubbing in Ghusl
Ruling on fard of washing body and dispute over rubbing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dalk in ghusl and explain why rubbing is not fard, using the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Water purifies by nature; mere contact suffices, so rubbing is not fard.

This lesson clarifies what exactly is obligatory in Ghusl. While there is consensus that washing the entire body is fard, the Hanafi school distinguishes itself by holding that rubbing (dalk) is not required. The proof is drawn from the Quran's description of water as intrinsically purifying. We will examine the reasoning and a brief comparison with the Maliki position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings stated
The passage states two things: (1) washing the body is fard, and (2) rubbing (dalk) is not fard. Note that the first is uncontroversial; the second is the disputed point.
The title of the lesson already hints at the dispute.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof for 'no dalk'
The author cites Quran 25:48, 'And We sent down from the sky purifying water.' The intensive form 'tahura' indicates water is intrinsically purifying. Hence, when water contacts an impure area, it purifies it without needing rubbing.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof).
3
Examine the Maliki counterargument
Imam Malik argues for dalk being fard by analogy (qiyas) to washing a garment: since ghusl is an action, it requires rubbing to be effective. Also, impurity in a garment is embedded and needs rubbing to dislodge it.
The passage presents this as the opposing view.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the analogy
The Hanafi response distinguishes between a garment and the skin. Impurity on the skin sits on the surface; water contact alone removes it because water is intrinsically purifying. In a garment, impurity penetrates the threads, requiring rubbing to remove it.
This refutes the Maliki qiyas.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical case
Consider a person who pours water over their body in ghusl without rubbing. According to Hanafi fiqh, the ghusl is valid because the fard of washing the body is fulfilled by the water reaching all parts. Rubbing is not required.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبدنه لا دلكه وإدخال الماء داخل الجلد للأقلف. أي لا يجب أي البدن [سنن الغسل] وسنته: أن يغسل يديه وفرجه ونجاسة لو كانت على بدنه، ثم يتوضأ ثم يُفيضُ الماء على بدنه ثلاثاً، ابتداء إلى رسغيه لئلا تشيع وبدنه [ أي وغسل بدنه ما يمكن فيغسل السرّة وبشرة اللحية ولو كثة، لو عبر بالجسد لكان أولى؛ لأن الأطراف داخلة في الجسد خارجة عن البدن؛ لأن البدن كما في "الدر"- من المنكب إلى الألية، والحاصل أنه يجب غسل ما يكون من ظاهر البدن ولو من وجه كالشارب والحاجب وجميع اللحية؛ إذ لا حرج فيه، وكذا الفرج الخارج لا ما فيه حرج بأن يتعسر إيصال الماء إليه أو يضر، كداخل العينين وباطن الجرح. (فتح) لا دلكه أي دلك البدن في الغسل ليس بفرض عندنا، وقال مالك: هو فرض؛ اعتباراً بغسل الثوب ولأن الغسل هو الفعل، ولا يكون إلا بالدلك، ولنا: أن الماء مطهر بطبعه؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَنْزَلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً طَهُورا (الفرقان:٤٨)، فإذا لاقى المحل النجس طهره، بخلاف الثوب؛ لأن النجاسة تخللت في أثنائه. (مستخلص)
And his body, not his rubbing, and introducing water under the skin for the uncircumcised. That is, it is not obligatory i.e., the body... [explanation] The rubbing of the body in ghusl is not fard according to us, and Malik said: it is fard; by analogy to washing a garment and because ghusl is an action and cannot be except by rubbing. Our proof: water is purifying by its nature, as Allah says: 'And We sent down from the sky purifying water' (25:48). So when it contacts the impure place, it purifies it, unlike the garment because impurity is embedded in its threads.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq states two rulings: washing the body is fard in ghusl, and rubbing is not. The commentary defines the body as from shoulder to buttocks, including the beard, mustache, and external genitals, but excluding areas of hardship. The Hanafi proof for rubbing not being required is water's intrinsic purifying quality (Quran 25:48). Malik's view that rubbing is obligatory is rejected because water alone suffices upon contact with the impurity, unlike a garment where rubbing is needed to dislodge embedded dirt.

Key Terms
دلك (dalk): Rubbing or scrubbing the body during ghusl
بدن (badan): The visible external body from shoulder to buttocks, including beard and external genitals

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is rubbing (dalk) of the body obligatory in ghusl?
A) Yes, it is fard.
B) No, it is not fard.
C) Only if impurity is visible.
D) Only for men.

Key Takeaway
Water's intrinsic purifying quality makes rubbing unnecessary in ghusl; only complete coverage of the body is fard.

The Foreskin (Qulfah) in Ghusl and Wudu: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on foreskin ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi views on the foreskin and apply the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling to ghusl and wudu scenarios.

Core Idea
The foreskin is outer skin for wudu but inner skin for ghusl — hardship eases ghusl, caution governs wudu.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the uncircumcised man's obligation to introduce water under the foreskin. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: some scholars treat the foreskin as entirely outer skin, requiring water to reach it in both ghusl and wudu. Others distinguish between ghusl (treated as inner skin) and wudu (treated as outer skin). The author of our commentary prefers the latter view, balancing hardship and caution. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is introducing water under the foreskin in ghusl/wudu. The issue: does the foreskin have the ruling of outer or inner skin?
The matn mentions إدخال الماء as part of the fara'id.
2
State the two positions
Some say the foreskin is outer in all respects; others say it is inner in ghusl and outer in wudu.
These are the views of different mashayikh.
3
Analyze the basis of each view
The first view treats the foreskin as part of the outer skin. The second considers the foreskin's natural covering as inner during ghusl due to hardship.
Hardship (حرج) is a key principle in the tarjih.
4
Understand the author's tarjih
The author chooses the dual ruling: hardship in ghusl (excusing water), caution in wudu (requiring water).
لمكان الحرج في الغسل وللاحتياط في الوضوء
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
For wudu, water must reach the foreskin; for ghusl, it is not obligatory.
This is the relied-upon position in the later Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإدخال الماء: عطف على قوله : لا دلكه، والأقلف هو الأغلف الذي لم يختن وفي وجوب إدخال الماء داخل الجلدة اختلاف المشايخ، فعند بعضهم لها حكم الظاهر من كل وجه حتى يجب إيصال الماء إليها، وإذا نزل البول ولم يخرج عنها نقض الوضوء، وعند البعض لها حكم الباطن في الغسل حتى لا يجب إيصال الماء إليها ينقض الوضوء بنزول البول إليها، فلها حكم الباطن في الغسل وحكم الظاهر في الوضوء عندهم، واختار المصنف هذا لمكان الحرج في الغسل وللاحتياط في الوضوء. (مستخلص)
And introducing water: conjunct to his saying: 'not his rubbing.' The aqlaf is the one who is uncircumcised. Regarding the obligation of introducing water inside the skin, there is a difference among the mashayikh. According to some, it has the ruling of the outer skin in every respect, so water must reach it, and if urine descends into it and does not exit, it breaks wudu. According to others, it has the ruling of the inner skin in ghusl, so water need not reach it, and urine descending into it does not break wudu. So it has the ruling of inner skin in ghusl and outer skin in wudu according to them. The author chose this due to hardship in ghusl and for caution in wudu.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of the foreskin (qulfah) for an uncircumcised man. The matn states that introducing water under the foreskin is part of the fara'id, but the commentary reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute. Some scholars treat the foreskin like outer skin, requiring water to reach it for both ghusl and wudu. Others treat it as inner skin for ghusl (not requiring water) but outer skin for wudu (requiring water). The author of the commentary (likely al-Zayla'i) prefers the latter view due to hardship in ghusl and caution in wudu. Thus, in the relied-upon position, water must be introduced into the foreskin for wudu but not for ghusl.

Key Terms
أقلف (aqlaf): An uncircumcised man; the foreskin is not removed.
جلدة (jildah): The skin of the foreskin (qulfah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi opinion, what is the ruling for an uncircumcised man regarding the foreskin in ghusl?
A) Water must reach the foreskin, as it is outer skin.
B) Water need not reach the foreskin, as it is inner skin.
C) The foreskin must be removed before ghusl.
D) Rubbing the foreskin is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the foreskin is outer skin for wudu (water must reach) but inner skin for ghusl (water not required) — a balanced application of hardship and caution.

Sunnah Acts of Ghusl in Detail
Listing the sunnah acts of ghusl with details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of ghusl and explain how they derive from the sunnan of wudu.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts of ghusl mirror those of wudu except facing qibla, and include pouring water three times.

Ghusl has obligatory components (fard) and recommended components (sunnah). This passage details the sunnah acts, drawing from a key Hanafi principle: whatever is sunnah in wudu is sunnah in ghusl, with one exception – facing the qibla. Understanding these acts helps you gain maximum reward in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The passage begins by stating that the sunnah acts of wudu are also sunnah in ghusl. Recognize this as a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh.
This principle is found in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
2
List the Common Sunnah Acts
Intention (niyyah) and pronouncing it are sunnah. Washing hands to wrists, washing private parts, and performing wudu as for prayer are also sunnah – except the feet if standing in water.
For feet: if in a pool of water, wash them after pouring water over the body.
3
Note the Exception
Facing the qibla is not sunnah in ghusl because it generally involves nudity. This is the sole exception to the general rule.
4
Describe the Pouring of Water
After wudu, the method of pouring water (ifadah) is sunnah: start with the right shoulder three times, then left shoulder three times, then head and entire body three times.
The water quantity is 8 ratls (approx. 2.5 liters). The procedure is based on the hadith of Maymunah.
5
Recognize the Hadith Source
The description is taken from the narration of Umm al-Mu'minin Maymunah about the Prophet's ghusl. This shows the sunnah acts are established prophetic practice.
The hadith is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسنته إلخ أي سنة الغسل أفاد في البحر: أن ما كان سنة في الوضوء فهو سنة في الغسل، فتسن فيه النية، ويندب التلفظ بها، وكذا يندب فيه ما هو مندوب في الوضوء سوى استقبال القبلة، فإنه يكون غالبا مع العورة وغسل اليدين؛ لأنهما آلة التطهير، ولقوله عليه: "فلا يغمسن يده في الإناء"، أما في غسل الفرج؛ فلأنه لا يخلو حال الجنابة عن النجاسة، وأما غسل النجاسة؛ لئلا تزداد بإصابة الماء. [كشف الحقائق: ١٢/١] فرجه وإن لم يكن به نجاسة. (ط) ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصلاة إلا رجليه إن كانا في مجمع الماء. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧/١] ثم يفيض الماء: أي المعهود في الشرع للغسل والوضوء، وهو ثمانية أرطال، وكيفية الإفاضة أن يبدأ بمنكبه الأيمن، فيفيض الماء عليه ثلاثاً، ثم بمنكبه الأيسر كذلك، ثم يفيض الماء على رأسه وسائر جسده كذلك. (مسكين وغيره) على بدنه [ أي يصب الماء على سائر أعضائه ثلاثاً، هكذا حكت أم المؤمنين ميمونة من غسل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. (مستخلص)]
And its sunnah etc., meaning the sunnah of ghusl. It is beneficial in al-Bahr: that whatever is sunnah in wudu is sunnah in ghusl. Thus intention is sunnah, and pronouncing it is recommended. Likewise, whatever is recommended in wudu is recommended in ghusl except facing the qibla, because it is often with the private parts, and washing the hands because they are instruments of purification, and because of his saying: 'Let him not dip his hand in the vessel.' As for washing the private parts, because the state of janabah is not free from impurity, and washing the impurity so that it does not increase with the water. Then he makes wudu like his wudu for prayer except his feet if he is in a pool of water. Then he pours water: the amount known in shari'ah for ghusl and wudu, which is eight ratls. The method of pouring is to start with his right shoulder, pouring water three times, then his left shoulder likewise, then he pours water on his head and all his body likewise. On his body, i.e., he pours water on all his limbs three times. Thus Umm al-Mu'minin Maymunah narrated the ghusl of the Messenger of Allah.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage lists the sunnah acts of ghusl as derived from the matn. The commentator notes that the sunnan of wudu apply to ghusl, except facing qibla due to nudity. The sunnan include: intention, pronouncing it, washing hands to the wrists, washing the private parts even if no visible impurity, wudu as for prayer (except feet if standing in water, then washing them after), then pouring water over the body three times starting with the right shoulder. The quantity of water is eight ratls (about 2.5 liters). The description is based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Maymunah.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): Recommended act in ghusl; omission does not invalidate but reward is missed.
إفاضة (ifadah): Pouring water over the body in a flowing manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the exception to the principle that 'whatever is sunnah in wudu is sunnah in ghusl'?
A) Washing hands to wrists
B) Facing the qibla
C) Performing wudu
D) Pouring water three times

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of ghusl are essentially those of wudu with the omission of qibla, plus the three-time pouring of water.

Ruling on Not Undoing Braids in Ghusl for Women
Ruling that a woman need not undo braids if water reaches roots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on undoing braids during ghusl for women and apply the condition of water reaching the roots to determine when it is required.

Core Idea
For women, undoing braids is not required if water reaches the roots; for men, it is required.

One of the practical concerns for women with braided hair is whether they must undo their braids during ghusl. This lesson, based on the Hanafi text, clarifies the ruling: the exemption from undoing braids is conditional upon water reaching the roots. We will examine the evidence from the hadith of Umm Salamah and understand why the ruling differs for men.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Subject
The act is performing ghusl (ritual bath) for a woman with braided hair. Determine who the ruling applies to.
The ruling specifically addresses women; men are treated differently.
2
State the Ruling and Condition
The ruling is that it is not obligatory (wajib) to undo braids if water reaches the roots of the hair. If water does NOT reach the roots, undoing becomes obligatory.
The condition (if its root is wetted) is explicit in the text.
3
Locate the Proof
The proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with her) where the Prophet ﷺ said: 'It suffices you if water reaches the roots of your hair.'
This is a specific concession (rukhsah) for women due to hardship.
4
Contrast with Men
Men who braid their hair are not exempt. They must ensure water reaches every part of the hair as a precaution, even if the roots are wetted.
The hadith specifically addressed a woman; men are under general obligation.
5
Apply to a Scenario
If a woman with braids pours water and is sure the roots are wetted, she need not undo braids. If only the braids are wetted, she must undo them.
Practical application requires verifying the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تنقض ضفيرة إن بل أصلها. والضفيرة الذؤابة من الضفر وهو فتل الشعر وإدخال بعضه في بعض. (البحر الرائق: ۱۲۰/۱)] أي لو بلت المرأة في الاغتسال أصل شعرها لم يجب عليها نقض ضفيرتها، ولا يجب عليها بل ذوائبها وهو الصحيح، وقيد بقوله: إن بل أصلها؛ لأنه إن لم يبل أصلها وجب النقض عليها، فذكر المرأة؛ لأن الرجل إذا ضفر شعر رأسه كالعلوي والتركي يجب إيصال الماء إلى أثناء شعر رأسه احتياطاً، وإن وصل الماء إلى ما تحتها؛ لأن النص في المرأة؛ لقوله للأم سلمة حين قالت: يا رسول الله ! إني امرأة أضفر رأسي، أفأنقضها إذا اغتسلت؟ قال: "يكفيك إذا بلغ الماء أصول شعرك" وللحرج في حقها. (مسكين، مستخلص)
And she does not undo a braid if its root reaches (water). The dafirah is the lock of hair from braiding, which is twisting hair and inserting some into others. Meaning, if the woman wets the root of her hair in ghusl, it is not obligatory upon her to undo her braid, and it is not obligatory upon her to wet the locks; this is the correct view. It is restricted by his saying: if its root is wetted, because if its root is not wetted, it is obligatory to undo it. The woman is mentioned because a man, if he braids his hair like a 'Alawi or Turk, must bring water to the inner part of his hair as a precaution, even if water reaches what is underneath it, because the text (hadith) is about women. He said to Umm Salamah when she said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair, shall I undo it when I perform ghusl? He said: 'It suffices you if water reaches the roots of your hair.' And due to hardship for her.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific ruling for women with braided hair. The matn states that a woman does not need to undo her braids (plait) provided that water reaches the roots. The commentary clarifies that if the roots are not wetted, the braids must be undone to ensure water reaches them. This exemption is specific to women, as established by the hadith of Umm Salamah. Men who braid their hair are not exempt; they must ensure water reaches even the inner strands, as a precaution. The ruling is based on the Prophet's explicit permission and the hardship women would face.

Key Terms
ضفيرة (dafirah): A braid or lock of hair that is twisted and interwoven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always
B) Never
C) Only if water does not reach the roots
D) Only if she made wudu first

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling exempts women from undoing braids during ghusl if water reaches the roots, based on the Prophet's concession to Umm Salamah and the principle of hardship.

Conditions for Ghusl: Dafq and Shahwah
Ruling that ghusl is fard only when semen exits with gushing and lust

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for ghusl due to seminal emission, explain the evidence from the hadith of Umm Salamah, and distinguish between the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and intra-Hanafi positions.

Core Idea
Ghusl is fard only when semen exits with gushing (dafq) and lust (shahwah); without these, no ghusl is required.

This lesson examines the precise conditions under which ghusl becomes obligatory due to seminal emission. The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith of Umm Salamah, ties the obligation to two specific characteristics: gushing and lust. We will explore the textual evidence, the intra-Hanafi differences, and the contrast with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its conditions
Identify that ghusl is fard (obligatory) when semen exits with two conditions: dafq (gushing) and shahwah (lust).
This is the core Hanafi position.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith of Umm Salamah: the Prophet asked 'Do you find lust?' and tied ghusl to it. This shows that lust is a necessary condition.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala according to Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's question indicates that ghusl is only required if pleasure is present. Without pleasure, there is no obligation.
This is a clear textual indication (dalala qati).
4
Identify the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i argues based on the general hadith 'al-ma'u al-ma'u' which he interprets as any emission of maniyy requires ghusl.
The Hanafi response interprets that hadith as referring to emission with lust, otherwise it would include madhi and wadi.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf considers the appearance of lust at the time of emission, not just the exit. Also, regarding residual semen, Abu Yusuf differs from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The mufta bihi is the majority view: exit with dafq and shahwah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرض عند مني ذي دفق وشهوة عند انفصاله، وتواري انفصاله أي وفرض عند تواري الحشفة. المعاني الموجبة للغسل. وفرض عند مني إلخ أي فرض الغسل مع نزول مني ذي دفق أي دفوق ولذة، فالخروج بدون الدفق والشهوة يوجب الغسل عندنا خلافاً للشافعي، له قوله عليه: "الماء الماء" يعني وجوب الاغتسال بإنزال المني، ولنا: ما من روت أم سلمة أنها سألت النبي له عن المرأة ترى في منامها مثل ما يرى الرجل، فقال عليه: "أتحد بذلك لذة" فقالت: نعم، فقال: "فلتغتسل علق الاغتسال باللذة وحديث الشافعي محمول على الإنزال بشهوة، وإنما حملنا الحديث على الخروج بشهوة؛ لأنه عام لا يمكن إجراؤه على العموم؛ لأنه يتناول المذي والودي والمني بشهوة وغير شهوة، والمني بالشهوة هو المراد بالإجماع. ذي دفق يقال: دفق الماء دفقا، صبّه صبا فيه دفع شدة. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٥/١] عند انفصاله متعلق بقوله: دفق وشهوة ]، أي فرض الغسل عند خروج مني موصوف بالدفق والشهوة عند محله عند الطرفين، وأما عند أبي يوسف فيعتبر ظهوره على وجه الشهوة أيضاً كما انفصال المني عن . كما إذا اغتسل قبل أن يبول، ثم سال عنه بقية المني يجب الغسل عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. (مسكين)
And it is fard at (the time of) semen characterized by gushing and lust at its separation, and at the disappearance of the glans. The meanings that necessitate ghusl. And fard at semen etc. i.e., ghusl is fard with the descent of semen with gushing and lust. So exit without gushing and lust necessitates ghusl according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His proof: his saying 'Water, water' meaning obligation of ghusl by emission of semen. Our proof: Umm Salamah reported that she asked the Prophet about a woman who sees in her dream what a man sees, and he said: 'Do you find lust from that?' She said yes. He said: 'Then let her perform ghusl.' He tied ghusl to lust. The hadith of al-Shafi'i is interpreted as emission with lust. We interpret the hadith as referring to exit with lust because it is general but cannot be applied generally, as it includes madhi, wadi, and semen with and without lust. Semen with lust is intended by consensus. Dafq: it is said dafaq al-ma'a dafqan, to pour it with force. At its separation relates to his saying: gushing and lust, i.e., ghusl is fard when semen described with gushing and lust exits. As for Abu Yusuf, he considers its appearance with lust as well, like the separation of semen... For example, if he bathed before urinating, then the remainder of semen flows out, ghusl is obligatory according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for ghusl becoming obligatory due to semen emission. The Hanafi position is that ghusl is only required when semen exits with gushing (dafq) and distinct sexual pleasure (shahwah). If it exits without these (e.g., due to illness or cold), ghusl is not obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf holds that even in such cases ghusl is required if it appears with lustful feelings. The Shafi'i position, based on a general hadith, is that any emission of maniyy necessitates ghusl. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of the Prophet instructing women with erotic dreams to perform ghusl ties ghusl to the experience of pleasure, and the general hadith is interpreted accordingly. There is also an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding residual semen after ghusl without urination: Abu Yusuf says no second ghusl, while the other two say yes if it exits with pleasure.

Key Terms
دفق (dafq): Gushing or forceful ejection of fluid.
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual pleasure or lust accompanying emission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, is ghusl required if semen exits without gushing and lust?
A) Yes, always
B) No, it is not required
C) Only if accompanied by a wet dream
D) Only for men

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires both gushing (dafq) and lust (shahwah) for ghusl to be fard upon seminal emission; without either, ghusl is not obligatory.

Obligation of Ghusl Upon Glans Disappearance
Ruling that ghusl is fard upon glans disappearance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that triggers obligatory ghusl after intercourse and apply it to various scenarios including exceptions.

Core Idea
Ghusl becomes fard when the glans disappears, regardless of emission.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq: when does sexual intercourse necessitate ghusl? The Hanafi position, supported by clear hadith, is that the mere disappearance of the glans into the private part of a living human is sufficient. Emission is not required. We will also explore exceptions when the partner is an animal or a corpse, and when intercourse occurs in non-standard locations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sexual intercourse. The ruling is that ghusl becomes fard (obligatory) upon disappearance of the glans.
Ghusl is fard 'ayn for both parties.
2
Locate the primary condition
The condition is 'tuwaree al-hashafah' – the glans (or its equivalent) must be concealed in the private part.
Applies to front and back private parts of a living human.
3
Understand the exceptions
If the partner is an animal or a dead body, ghusl is not obligatory without emission. Also, if intimacy occurs in non-private areas (e.g., thigh), no ghusl without emission.
Reason: lack of full desire (in animals/dead) or not the intended place.
4
Examine the dalil
The hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl is obligatory, whether he emitted or not.' This is the primary proof.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning.
5
Apply to both parties
Ghusl is obligatory on both the man and the woman, as the text explicitly includes 'al-faa'il wa al-maf'ool'.
Both are legally responsible (mukallaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتواري الحشفة أو قدرها من مقطوعه، وقوله : "في قبل أو "دبر" أي المتحققين من آدمي، حتى لو كان بهيمة أو ميتة لا يجب الغسل بدون الإنزال ؛ لقصور الداعي فيهما، والوجوب لقوله عليه: "إذا التقى الختانان وتوارت الحشفة وجب الغسل، أنزل أو لم ينزل"؛ ولأنه سبب الإنزال، فيقام سبب الظاهر مقامه كنوم المضطجع، وإنما قيل بالقبل والدبر ؛ لأنه لو جامع امرأته في ما دونهما كالسرة والفخذ وتوارت الحشفة لم يجب الغسل ما لم ينزل، وقوله: "عليهما" أي على الفاعل والمفعول، أي الرجل والمرأة المكلفين، والدليل على وجوب الغسل بمجرد تغيب الحشفة في القبل وإن لم ينزل حديث أبي هريرة له أنه عليه قال: "إذا جلس بين شعبها الأربع ثم جهدها فقد وجب الغسل، وصح عن عائشة لها أنها قالت: "إذا جاوز الختان الختان وجب الغسل"، =
And the disappearance of the glans or its measure for one whose glans is cut off, and his statement: 'in the front or the back' meaning the confirmed private parts of a human. Even if it were an animal or a corpse, ghusl is not obligatory without emission because of the deficiency of desire in both. And obligation due to his saying: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl is obligatory, whether he emitted or not.' And because it is a cause of emission, so the apparent cause is established in its place like the sleep of one reclining. It is only said with regard to the front and back because if he had intercourse with his wife in other than these, like the navel or thigh, and the glans disappeared, ghusl is not obligatory unless he emitted. And his statement: 'upon both' means upon the doer and the recipient, i.e., the man and the woman who are legally responsible. The evidence for the obligation of ghusl simply by the disappearance of the glans in the front even without emission is the hadith of Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'When he sits between her four parts and then exerts himself, ghusl becomes obligatory.' And it is authentic from Aisha that she said: 'When the circumcised part passes the circumcised part, ghusl becomes obligatory.'
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage discusses the second cause of ghusl: sexual intercourse. The matn states that ghusl is fard when the glans (or its equivalent in a mutilated man) disappears into the private part (front or back) of a living human being. If the partner is an animal or a dead body, ghusl is not obligatory without emission due to lack of full sexual desire. The proof is the hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl is obligatory, whether he emitted or not.' This establishes the principle that penetration alone necessitates ghusl. The commentary also notes that if intercourse occurs in non-standard places (like thigh), ghusl is only required if emission occurs. Both partners (male and female) are required to perform ghusl.

Key Terms
حشفة (hashafah): The glans of the penis; the part that must disappear for ghusl to be fard.
ختان (khatan): The circumcised part of the male and female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is ghusl obligatory due to intercourse?
A) Only if emission occurs
B) When the glans disappears into the private part, even without emission
C) Only if intercourse is with a living human
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Ghusl becomes fard upon glans disappearance, even without emission; exceptions apply for non-human partners and non-standard locations.

Primary Causes of Ghusl: Maniy and Genital Contact
Establishes the two major causes of ghusl and their proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two primary causes of obligatory ghusl (janabah) and explain the Hanafi proofs and the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the anus.

Core Idea
Ghusl becomes obligatory either by emission of maniy with pleasure or by concealment of the glans in the front or back (according to the Sahibayn).

This lesson covers the two main triggers for janabah ghusl: the emission of semen (maniy) with dafaq and shahwa, and the meeting of circumcised parts (al-khitanayn). You will learn the Hanafi reliance on the hadith of Umm Salama and the response to the Shafi'i 'Water is from water' argument. The intra-Hanafi difference on the anus is also explored.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary causes
Locate in the text the two conditions: (1) maniy with dafaq and shahwa, (2) concealment of the hashafah in the front or back.
Both trigger janabah and require ghusl.
2
Examine the proof for maniy
Read the hadith of Umm Salama linking ghusl to pleasure (al-ladhdha) and the Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i hadith.
Hadith 'Water is from water' is restricted by the specifying hadith.
3
Analyse the proof for concealment
Study the hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet…' and the qiyas from front to back.
The hadith covers both front and back according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify Abu Hanifa's exception for the back (anus) and the Sahibayn's response using qiyas and the hadd argument.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
5
Apply the ruling to real-life
Consider a scenario: if a man inserts his glans into his wife's anus without ejaculation, ghusl is wajib according to the mufta bihi.
