كتاب الطهارة

المعاني الموجبة للغسل

ولا تنقض ضفيرة إن بل أصلها. (البحر الرائق: ۱۲۰/۱)] أي لو بلت المرأة في الاغتسال أصل شعرها لم يجب عليها نقض ضفيرتها، ولا يجب عليها بل ذوائبها وهو الصحيح، وقيد بقوله: إن بل أصلها؛ لأنه إن لم يبل أصلها وجب النقض عليها، فذكر المرأة؛ لأن الرجل إذا ضفر شعر رأسه كالعلوي والتركي يجب إيصال الماء إلى أثناء شعر رأسه احتياطاً، وإن وصل الماء إلى ما تحتها؛ لأن النص في المرأة؛ لقوله للأم سلمة حين قالت: يا رسول الله ! إني امرأة أضفر رأسي، أفأنقضها إذا اغتسلت؟ قال: "يكفيك إذا بلغ الماء أصول شعرك" وللحرج في حقها. (مسكين، مستخلص) وفرض عند مني إلخ أي فرض الغسل مع نزول مني ذي دفق أي دفوق ولذة، فالخروج بدون الدفق والشهوة يوجب الغسل عندنا خلافاً للشافعي، له قوله عليه: "الماء الماء" يعني وجوب الاغتسال بإنزال المني، ولنا: ما من روت أم سلمة أنها سألت النبي عن المرأة ترى في منامها مثل ما يرى الرجل، فقال عليه: "أتحد بذلك لذة" فقالت: نعم، فقال: "فلتغتسل" علق الاغتسال باللذة وحديث الشافعي محمول على الإنزال بشهوة، وإنما حملنا الحديث على الخروج بشهوة؛ لأنه عام لا يمكن إجراؤه على العموم؛ لأنه يتناول المذي والودي والمني بشهوة وغير شهوة، والمني يعتبر انفصاله بالشهوة هو المراد بالإجماع. ذي دفق يقال: دفق الماء دفقا، صبّه صبا فيه دفع شدة. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٥/١] عند انفصاله متعلق بقوله: دفق وشهوة ]، أي فرض الغسل عند خروج مني موصوف بالدفق والشهوة عند محله عند الطرفين، وأما عند أبي يوسف فيعتبر ظهوره على وجه الشهوة أيضاً كما انفصال المني عن . كما إذا اغتسل قبل أن يبول، ثم سال عنه بقية المني يجب الغسل عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. (مسكين) وتواري إلخ التواري الغيبوبة والحشفة ما فوق الختان، أي موضع القطع من الذكر والأنثى، يعني فرض الغسل عند تغيب الحشفة أو قدرها من مقطوعه، وقوله : "في قبل أو دبر" أي المتحققين من آدمي، حتى لو كان بهيمة أو ميتة لا يجب الغسل بدون الإنزال ؛ لقصور الداعي فيهما، والوجوب لقوله عليه: "إذا التقى الختانان وتوارت الحشفة وجب الغسل، أنزل أو لم ينزل"؛ ولأنه سبب الإنزال، فيقام سبب الظاهر مقامه كنوم المضطجع، وإنما قيل بالقبل والدبر ؛ لأنه لو جامع امرأته في ما دونهما كالسرة والفخذ وتوارت الحشفة لم يجب الغسل ما لم ينزل، وقوله: "عليهما" أي على الفاعل والمفعول، أي الرجل والمرأة المكلفين، والدليل على وجوب الغسل بمجرد تغيب الحشفة في القبل وإن لم ينزل حديث أبي هريرة أنه عليه قال: "إذا جلس بين شعبها الأربع ثم جهدها فقد وجب الغسل"، وصح عن عائشة لها أنها قالت: "إذا جاوز الختان الختان وجب الغسل"، وأما في صورة الدبر فعند أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ لأنه لما وجب الحد الذي يحتاط في تركه فلأن يجب الغسل أولى، وأما عند أبي حنيفة فلأن الاحتياط في الحد تركه؛ لأنه من العقوبات، وفي إيجاب الغسل احتياط؛ لأنه من العبادات. (فتح، مسكين وغيره) حشفة: هي ما فوق الختان ولو بحائل توجد معه الحرارة على الأصح. (ط) عليهما أي الفاعل والمفعول لو مكلفين، فلو أحدهما مكلفا فعليه فقط وإن لم ينزل . (ط) وحيض ونفاس أي فرض الغسل عند انقطاع حيض ونفاس. (ط) لا مذي إلخ عطف على "منى"، أي لا يغسل عند خروج مذي وهو الذي يخرج عند الملاعبة ولا ودي، ولا عند احتلام، وهو ما يرى النائم من الجماع بلا بلل مطلقا، سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة، وقال محمد: على المرأة الغسل احتياطاً إذا التذت لذة الإنزال، أما من استيقظ فوجد على فراشه أو فخذه بللاً وهو يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه مني أو شك فعليه الغسل، أما إذا لم يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه مني أو شك فكذلك، وإن تيقن أنه مذي فلا غسل عليه، وإذا استيقظ فوجد في إحليله بللاً ولم يتذكر حلماً إن كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا غسل عليه، وإن كان ساكناً فعليه الغسل، هذا إذا نام قائما أو قاعدا، أما إذا نام مضطجعاً وتيقن أنه مني فعليه الغسل، فهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وإن استيقظ الرجل والمرأة فوجدا منياً على الفراش، وكل واحد منهما ينكر الاحتلام وجب عليهما الغسل، وقال بعضهم: إن كان المني طويلاً أو أبيض فعلى الرجل، وإن كان مدوراً أو أصفر فعلى المرأة. (مسكين) وودي هو بول غليظ أبيض يتعقب الرقيق منه. (ط) وسن للجمعة إلخ : أي سن الغسل لأجل الجمعة وغيرها، وقيل: هذه الأربعة مستحبة، وسمى محمد الغسل في الجمعة حسناً في "الأصل"، وقال مالك: هو واجب وقال بعض الشارحين: إنه غير صحيح؛ فإنه لم يقل بالوجوب إلا أهل الظاهر، ودليلهم قوله عليه: "غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم"، والجواب أنه منسوخ أو هو من باب انتهاء الحكم لانتهاء العلة؛ لأن الناس كانوا يلبسون الصوف وكان مسجدهم ضيقاً، فخرج عليها في يوم حار وعرق الناس في ذلك الصوف حتى ظهرت منه رياح ثم كثر الخير ولبسوا غير الصوف ووسع مسجدهم، أو المراد بالواجب الثابت. (مسكين) والإحرام: أي عند إحرام الحج والعمرة. (ط) وعرفة: أي يوم عرفة؛ لورود السنة بذلك. ووجب للميت لقوله عليه: "للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق: إذا دعاه أن يجيبه، وإذا مرض أن يعوده، وإذا مات أن يحضره، وإذا لقيه أن يسلم عليه، وإذا استنصحه أن ينصحه، وإذا عطس أن يشمته"، فقوله: إذا مات أن يحضره يدل على الغسل وغيره من كل ما تعلق بتجهيز الميت، وقيل: غسل الميت سنة مؤكدة، وفي "الوافي" الغسل بعد الموت فرض. (فتح، مسكين) يوم
Book of Purification. The meanings that necessitate ghusl. And she does not undo her braid if its root becomes wet. (From al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/120) Meaning: If a woman wets the root of her hair while bathing, she is not obligated to undo her braid, and she is not obligated to wet the locks; this is the correct view. It is restricted by his saying 'if its root becomes wet' because if its root does not become wet, she must undo it. The mention of the woman is because if a man braids his hair like an Alawi or Turk, he must deliver water to the inside of his hair as a precaution, even if water reaches beneath it, because the text is for the woman, due to his statement to Umm Salama when she said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair; should I undo it when I bathe?' He said, 'It suffices you if water reaches the roots of your hair' and due to hardship for her. (Miskeen, Mustakhlas) And obligatory upon maniy etc. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory with the descent of maniy that has dafaq (gushing) and shahwa (pleasure). So emission without dafaq and shahwa necessitates ghusl according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He has his statement: 'Water is from water' meaning obligation of ghusl by the emission of maniy. And we have what Umm Salama narrated that she asked the Prophet about a woman who sees in her dream what a man sees. He said, 'Do you experience pleasure from that?' She said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Then let her bathe.' He attached ghusl to pleasure. And the hadith of al-Shafi'i is interpreted as emission with shahwa. We interpreted the hadith as emission with shahwa because it is general and cannot be applied generally because it includes madhi, wadi, and maniy with and without shahwa, and maniy whose separation is with shahwa is intended by consensus. 'Dafaq' is said: he poured water pouring it, pouring it with force. (al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/125) 'At its separation' is attached to his saying 'dafaq and shahwa'. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory at the emanation of maniy described with gushing and shahwa at its place according to both sides. As for Abu Yusuf, he considers its appearance with shahwa as well as the separation of maniy? Just as if he bathed before urinating, then the remainder of maniy flowed, ghusl is obligatory according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Hanifa. (Miskeen) And concealment etc. al-Tawari is disappearance, and al-Hashafah is what is above the circumcision, i.e., the place of cutting from the male and female. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory upon concealment of the glans or its equivalent from one whose glans is cut off, and his saying 'in the front or back' means actual ones from a human. Even if it were an animal or a corpse, ghusl is not obligatory without emission because of lack of desire. And obligation is due to his statement: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans becomes concealed, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' And because it is a cause of emission, so the apparent cause is established in its place like the sleep of one lying on his side. And it was said only with front and back because if he had intercourse with his wife in other than them, like the navel and thigh, and the glans became concealed, ghusl is not obligatory unless he ejaculates. And his saying 'upon both' means upon the doer and the recipient, i.e., the man and the woman who are legally responsible. And the evidence for the obligation of ghusl by mere concealment of the glans in the front even if he does not ejaculate is the hadith of Abu Hurayra that he said: 'When he sits between her four branches and then exerts himself, ghusl becomes obligatory.' And it is authentic from Aisha that she said: 'When the circumcision passes the circumcision, ghusl becomes obligatory.' As for the case of the back, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because when the hadd becomes obligatory, which one is cautious in avoiding, so the obligation of ghusl is more appropriate. And according to Abu Hanifa, caution in the hadd is its avoidance because it is a punishment, and in obligating ghusl is caution because it is an act of worship. (Fath, Miskeen, etc.) al-Hashafah: It is what is above the circumcision even with a barrier that is accompanied by heat according to the correct view. (T) 'upon both' means the doer and recipient if they are legally responsible; if one of them is legally responsible, then only upon him even if he does not ejaculate. (T) And hayd and nifas: meaning ghusl is obligatory at the cessation of hayd and nifas. (T) Not madhi etc. is conjuncted to 'maniy', meaning: ghusl is not required upon emission of madhi, which is emitted during foreplay, nor wadi, nor upon a wet dream, which is what a sleeper sees of intercourse without any wetness, whether man or woman. And Muhammad said: upon the woman, ghusl is obligatory as a precaution if she experiences the pleasure of ejaculation. As for one who wakes up and finds wetness on his bedding or thigh and he remembers a wet dream and is certain it is maniy or is in doubt, he must perform ghusl. As for if he does not remember a wet dream and is certain it is maniy or is in doubt, likewise. And if he is certain it is madhi, then no ghusl upon him. And if he wakes up and finds wetness in his urethra and does not remember a dream, if his private part was erect before sleep, no ghusl upon him; if it was limp, then ghusl is upon him. This is if he slept standing or sitting. As for if he slept lying down and is certain it is maniy, then ghusl is upon him. This issue occurs frequently and people are negligent of it. And if a man and woman wake up and find maniy on the bedding, and each of them denies a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory upon both. And some said: if the maniy is long or white, then upon the man; if it is round or yellow, then upon the woman. (Miskeen) And wadi is thick white urine that follows the thin urine. (T) And sunnah for Friday etc.: meaning: ghusl for Friday and others is sunnah. And it was said: these four are recommended. Muhammad called ghusl on Friday 'good' in al-Asl. Malik said it is obligatory. And some commentators said this is incorrect; only the Zahiris said it is obligatory. Their evidence is his statement: 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person.' The answer is that it is abrogated or it is from the category of termination of ruling due to termination of cause, because the people used to wear wool and their mosque was narrow, so he went out on a hot day and the people sweated in that wool until odors appeared from it. Then prosperity increased and they wore other than wool and their mosque was expanded. Or what is meant by 'obligatory' is established. (Miskeen) And al-Ihram: meaning when entering ihram for hajj and umra. (T) And Arafah: meaning the day of Arafah, because the sunna has come for that. And obligatory for the deceased due to his statement: 'For the Muslim upon the Muslim are six rights: if he invites him, he should respond; if he is sick, he should visit him; if he dies, he should attend him; if he meets him, he should greet him; if he seeks his advice, he should advise him; if he sneezes, he should say yarhamuk Allah.' So his saying 'if he dies, he should attend him' indicates ghusl and everything related to preparing the deceased. And it was said: ghusl of the deceased is a strongly recommended sunnah. And in al-Wafi, ghusl after death is fard. (Fath, Miskeen)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings on ghusl (obligatory bath) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins with the issue of a woman's braided hair: if water reaches the roots, she need not undo her braids, based on the hadith of Umm Salama and to avoid hardship. Then it addresses the causes that necessitate ghusl: (1) Emission of maniy (semen) that exits with gushing flow (dafaq) and pleasure (shahwa). This is the Hanafi position; without dafaq and shahwa, ghusl is still obligatory, but they attach it to pleasure based on the hadith of Umm Salama linking ghusl to pleasure. The Shafi'i school holds that any emission of maniy necessitates ghusl, but the Hanafis rebut by specifying the hadith 'Water is from water' to emission with shahwa. (2) Meeting of the circumcised parts (glans entering the vagina or anus) even without ejaculation, based on the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory.' There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the anus: Abu Hanifa does not consider mere insertion into the anus sufficient for ghusl without emission, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) do, by qiyas on the front and because the hadd (for sodomy) is more severe.

The passage then covers ghusl due to hayd (menses) and nifas (postpartum bleeding) after they cease. It clarifies that madhi (prostatic fluid) and wadi (thick discharge) do not require ghusl, contradicting some views. Wet dreams without wetness also do not require ghusl. Various scenarios of finding wetness upon waking are detailed, including the distinction between maniy and madhi, and the ruling if both a man and woman find maniy on the bedding.

Finally, it lists recommended (sunnah) ghusl: for Friday, the two Eids, for ihram, and on the day of Arafah. Ghusl for the deceased is considered obligatory (fard) by some, or sunnah mu'akkadah by others; the text presents the view that it is obligatory based on the hadith of the six rights. The passage thus lays out the complete fiqh of ghusl according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual full-body bath required to remove major ritual impurity (janabah).
مني (maniy): Semen, the fluid emitted at orgasm. Its emission with shahwa necessitates ghusl.
حشفة (hashafah): Glans of the penis or clitoris; the part above the circumcision. Its concealment in the front or back necessitates ghusl.
دفق (dafaq): Gushing flow of fluid; characteristic of maniy.
لذة (ladhdha): Pleasure; specifically the pleasurable sensation at the moment of emission of maniy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi view, is ghusl obligatory for a man who inserts his glans into his wife's anus without ejaculation?
A) Yes, because the hadith covers both front and back.
B) No, because Abu Hanifa said it is not obligatory.
C) Yes, only if he ejaculates.
D) No, because it is not a sexual organ.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl becomes obligatory from two causes: maniy with pleasure and concealment of the glans; the mufta bihi includes the anus.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Ghusl from Menstruation, Postpartum Bleeding, and Related Fluids
Details rulings on ghusl from hayd, nifas, madhi, wadi, and wet dreams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rulings for ghusl due to hayd, nifas, madhi, wadi, and dream-related emissions, and apply the Hanafi rules concerning certainty.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory after hayd and nifas; madhi and wadi do not require ghusl; wet dreams require ghusl only if liquid is emitted with certainty.

This lesson covers the remaining causes of obligatory ghusl: the cessation of menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). It also clarifies that prostatic fluid (madhi) and thick discharge (wadi) do not require ghusl. The section on wet dreams details when ghusl is necessary, emphasizing the importance of certainty and distinguishing between maniy and madhi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory ghusl from hayd and nifas
The passage states that ghusl is fard upon cessation of hayd and nifas. Note that the text does not discuss the duration or minimum period, only the obligation.
This is agreed upon across schools.
2
Distinguish fluids that do not require ghusl
Read the list: madhi (emitted during foreplay), wadi (thick white urine), and wet dreams without wetness do not require ghusl.
Madhi and wadi only require washing the area and wudu, not ghusl.
3
Analyse the scenario of finding wetness upon waking
Study the detailed scenarios: if one finds wetness and remembers a wet dream, ghusl is required. If no dream but certain it is maniy, ghusl required. If certain it is madhi, no ghusl. If uncertain, no ghusl.
The text provides specific rules for erect vs. limp state and sleeping position.
4
Apply the rule of certainty
Certainty of maniy requires ghusl; doubt does not. The passage also covers joint finding of maniy on bedding.
If a couple finds maniy and both deny dreaming, both must do ghusl.

كتاب الطهارة

المعاني الموجبة للغسل

ولا تنقض ضفيرة إن بل أصلها. (البحر الرائق: ۱۲۰/۱)] أي لو بلت المرأة في الاغتسال أصل شعرها لم يجب عليها نقض ضفيرتها، ولا يجب عليها بل ذوائبها وهو الصحيح، وقيد بقوله: إن بل أصلها؛ لأنه إن لم يبل أصلها وجب النقض عليها، فذكر المرأة؛ لأن الرجل إذا ضفر شعر رأسه كالعلوي والتركي يجب إيصال الماء إلى أثناء شعر رأسه احتياطاً، وإن وصل الماء إلى ما تحتها؛ لأن النص في المرأة؛ لقوله للأم سلمة حين قالت: يا رسول الله ! إني امرأة أضفر رأسي، أفأنقضها إذا اغتسلت؟ قال: "يكفيك إذا بلغ الماء أصول شعرك" وللحرج في حقها. (مسكين، مستخلص) وفرض عند مني إلخ أي فرض الغسل مع نزول مني ذي دفق أي دفوق ولذة، فالخروج بدون الدفق والشهوة يوجب الغسل عندنا خلافاً للشافعي، له قوله عليه: "الماء الماء" يعني وجوب الاغتسال بإنزال المني، ولنا: ما من روت أم سلمة أنها سألت النبي عن المرأة ترى في منامها مثل ما يرى الرجل، فقال عليه: "أتحد بذلك لذة" فقالت: نعم، فقال: "فلتغتسل" علق الاغتسال باللذة وحديث الشافعي محمول على الإنزال بشهوة، وإنما حملنا الحديث على الخروج بشهوة؛ لأنه عام لا يمكن إجراؤه على العموم؛ لأنه يتناول المذي والودي والمني بشهوة وغير شهوة، والمني يعتبر انفصاله بالشهوة هو المراد بالإجماع. ذي دفق يقال: دفق الماء دفقا، صبّه صبا فيه دفع شدة. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٥/١] عند انفصاله متعلق بقوله: دفق وشهوة ]، أي فرض الغسل عند خروج مني موصوف بالدفق والشهوة عند محله عند الطرفين، وأما عند أبي يوسف فيعتبر ظهوره على وجه الشهوة أيضاً كما انفصال المني عن . كما إذا اغتسل قبل أن يبول، ثم سال عنه بقية المني يجب الغسل عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. (مسكين) وتواري إلخ التواري الغيبوبة والحشفة ما فوق الختان، أي موضع القطع من الذكر والأنثى، يعني فرض الغسل عند تغيب الحشفة أو قدرها من مقطوعه، وقوله : "في قبل أو دبر" أي المتحققين من آدمي، حتى لو كان بهيمة أو ميتة لا يجب الغسل بدون الإنزال ؛ لقصور الداعي فيهما، والوجوب لقوله عليه: "إذا التقى الختانان وتوارت الحشفة وجب الغسل، أنزل أو لم ينزل"؛ ولأنه سبب الإنزال، فيقام سبب الظاهر مقامه كنوم المضطجع، وإنما قيل بالقبل والدبر ؛ لأنه لو جامع امرأته في ما دونهما كالسرة والفخذ وتوارت الحشفة لم يجب الغسل ما لم ينزل، وقوله: "عليهما" أي على الفاعل والمفعول، أي الرجل والمرأة المكلفين، والدليل على وجوب الغسل بمجرد تغيب الحشفة في القبل وإن لم ينزل حديث أبي هريرة أنه عليه قال: "إذا جلس بين شعبها الأربع ثم جهدها فقد وجب الغسل"، وصح عن عائشة لها أنها قالت: "إذا جاوز الختان الختان وجب الغسل"، وأما في صورة الدبر فعند أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ لأنه لما وجب الحد الذي يحتاط في تركه فلأن يجب الغسل أولى، وأما عند أبي حنيفة فلأن الاحتياط في الحد تركه؛ لأنه من العقوبات، وفي إيجاب الغسل احتياط؛ لأنه من العبادات. (فتح، مسكين وغيره) حشفة: هي ما فوق الختان ولو بحائل توجد معه الحرارة على الأصح. (ط) عليهما أي الفاعل والمفعول لو مكلفين، فلو أحدهما مكلفا فعليه فقط وإن لم ينزل . (ط) وحيض ونفاس أي فرض الغسل عند انقطاع حيض ونفاس. (ط) لا مذي إلخ عطف على "منى"، أي لا يغسل عند خروج مذي وهو الذي يخرج عند الملاعبة ولا ودي، ولا عند احتلام، وهو ما يرى النائم من الجماع بلا بلل مطلقا، سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة، وقال محمد: على المرأة الغسل احتياطاً إذا التذت لذة الإنزال، أما من استيقظ فوجد على فراشه أو فخذه بللاً وهو يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه مني أو شك فعليه الغسل، أما إذا لم يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه مني أو شك فكذلك، وإن تيقن أنه مذي فلا غسل عليه، وإذا استيقظ فوجد في إحليله بللاً ولم يتذكر حلماً إن كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا غسل عليه، وإن كان ساكناً فعليه الغسل، هذا إذا نام قائما أو قاعدا، أما إذا نام مضطجعاً وتيقن أنه مني فعليه الغسل، فهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وإن استيقظ الرجل والمرأة فوجدا منياً على الفراش، وكل واحد منهما ينكر الاحتلام وجب عليهما الغسل، وقال بعضهم: إن كان المني طويلاً أو أبيض فعلى الرجل، وإن كان مدوراً أو أصفر فعلى المرأة. (مسكين) وودي هو بول غليظ أبيض يتعقب الرقيق منه. (ط) وسن للجمعة إلخ : أي سن الغسل لأجل الجمعة وغيرها، وقيل: هذه الأربعة مستحبة، وسمى محمد الغسل في الجمعة حسناً في "الأصل"، وقال مالك: هو واجب وقال بعض الشارحين: إنه غير صحيح؛ فإنه لم يقل بالوجوب إلا أهل الظاهر، ودليلهم قوله عليه: "غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم"، والجواب أنه منسوخ أو هو من باب انتهاء الحكم لانتهاء العلة؛ لأن الناس كانوا يلبسون الصوف وكان مسجدهم ضيقاً، فخرج عليها في يوم حار وعرق الناس في ذلك الصوف حتى ظهرت منه رياح ثم كثر الخير ولبسوا غير الصوف ووسع مسجدهم، أو المراد بالواجب الثابت. (مسكين) والإحرام: أي عند إحرام الحج والعمرة. (ط) وعرفة: أي يوم عرفة؛ لورود السنة بذلك. ووجب للميت لقوله عليه: "للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق: إذا دعاه أن يجيبه، وإذا مرض أن يعوده، وإذا مات أن يحضره، وإذا لقيه أن يسلم عليه، وإذا استنصحه أن ينصحه، وإذا عطس أن يشمته"، فقوله: إذا مات أن يحضره يدل على الغسل وغيره من كل ما تعلق بتجهيز الميت، وقيل: غسل الميت سنة مؤكدة، وفي "الوافي" الغسل بعد الموت فرض. (فتح، مسكين) يوم
Book of Purification. The meanings that necessitate ghusl. And she does not undo her braid if its root becomes wet. (From al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/120) Meaning: If a woman wets the root of her hair while bathing, she is not obligated to undo her braid, and she is not obligated to wet the locks; this is the correct view. It is restricted by his saying 'if its root becomes wet' because if its root does not become wet, she must undo it. The mention of the woman is because if a man braids his hair like an Alawi or Turk, he must deliver water to the inside of his hair as a precaution, even if water reaches beneath it, because the text is for the woman, due to his statement to Umm Salama when she said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair; should I undo it when I bathe?' He said, 'It suffices you if water reaches the roots of your hair' and due to hardship for her. (Miskeen, Mustakhlas) And obligatory upon maniy etc. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory with the descent of maniy that has dafaq (gushing) and shahwa (pleasure). So emission without dafaq and shahwa necessitates ghusl according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He has his statement: 'Water is from water' meaning obligation of ghusl by the emission of maniy. And we have what Umm Salama narrated that she asked the Prophet about a woman who sees in her dream what a man sees. He said, 'Do you experience pleasure from that?' She said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Then let her bathe.' He attached ghusl to pleasure. And the hadith of al-Shafi'i is interpreted as emission with shahwa. We interpreted the hadith as emission with shahwa because it is general and cannot be applied generally because it includes madhi, wadi, and maniy with and without shahwa, and maniy whose separation is with shahwa is intended by consensus. 'Dafaq' is said: he poured water pouring it, pouring it with force. (al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/125) 'At its separation' is attached to his saying 'dafaq and shahwa'. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory at the emanation of maniy described with gushing and shahwa at its place according to both sides. As for Abu Yusuf, he considers its appearance with shahwa as well as the separation of maniy? Just as if he bathed before urinating, then the remainder of maniy flowed, ghusl is obligatory according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Hanifa. (Miskeen) And concealment etc. al-Tawari is disappearance, and al-Hashafah is what is above the circumcision, i.e., the place of cutting from the male and female. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory upon concealment of the glans or its equivalent from one whose glans is cut off, and his saying 'in the front or back' means actual ones from a human. Even if it were an animal or a corpse, ghusl is not obligatory without emission because of lack of desire. And obligation is due to his statement: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans becomes concealed, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' And because it is a cause of emission, so the apparent cause is established in its place like the sleep of one lying on his side. And it was said only with front and back because if he had intercourse with his wife in other than them, like the navel and thigh, and the glans became concealed, ghusl is not obligatory unless he ejaculates. And his saying 'upon both' means upon the doer and the recipient, i.e., the man and the woman who are legally responsible. And the evidence for the obligation of ghusl by mere concealment of the glans in the front even if he does not ejaculate is the hadith of Abu Hurayra that he said: 'When he sits between her four branches and then exerts himself, ghusl becomes obligatory.' And it is authentic from Aisha that she said: 'When the circumcision passes the circumcision, ghusl becomes obligatory.' As for the case of the back, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because when the hadd becomes obligatory, which one is cautious in avoiding, so the obligation of ghusl is more appropriate. And according to Abu Hanifa, caution in the hadd is its avoidance because it is a punishment, and in obligating ghusl is caution because it is an act of worship. (Fath, Miskeen, etc.) al-Hashafah: It is what is above the circumcision even with a barrier that is accompanied by heat according to the correct view. (T) 'upon both' means the doer and recipient if they are legally responsible; if one of them is legally responsible, then only upon him even if he does not ejaculate. (T) And hayd and nifas: meaning ghusl is obligatory at the cessation of hayd and nifas. (T) Not madhi etc. is conjuncted to 'maniy', meaning: ghusl is not required upon emission of madhi, which is emitted during foreplay, nor wadi, nor upon a wet dream, which is what a sleeper sees of intercourse without any wetness, whether man or woman. And Muhammad said: upon the woman, ghusl is obligatory as a precaution if she experiences the pleasure of ejaculation. As for one who wakes up and finds wetness on his bedding or thigh and he remembers a wet dream and is certain it is maniy or is in doubt, he must perform ghusl. As for if he does not remember a wet dream and is certain it is maniy or is in doubt, likewise. And if he is certain it is madhi, then no ghusl upon him. And if he wakes up and finds wetness in his urethra and does not remember a dream, if his private part was erect before sleep, no ghusl upon him; if it was limp, then ghusl is upon him. This is if he slept standing or sitting. As for if he slept lying down and is certain it is maniy, then ghusl is upon him. This issue occurs frequently and people are negligent of it. And if a man and woman wake up and find maniy on the bedding, and each of them denies a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory upon both. And some said: if the maniy is long or white, then upon the man; if it is round or yellow, then upon the woman. (Miskeen) And wadi is thick white urine that follows the thin urine. (T) And sunnah for Friday etc.: meaning: ghusl for Friday and others is sunnah. And it was said: these four are recommended. Muhammad called ghusl on Friday 'good' in al-Asl. Malik said it is obligatory. And some commentators said this is incorrect; only the Zahiris said it is obligatory. Their evidence is his statement: 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person.' The answer is that it is abrogated or it is from the category of termination of ruling due to termination of cause, because the people used to wear wool and their mosque was narrow, so he went out on a hot day and the people sweated in that wool until odors appeared from it. Then prosperity increased and they wore other than wool and their mosque was expanded. Or what is meant by 'obligatory' is established. (Miskeen) And al-Ihram: meaning when entering ihram for hajj and umra. (T) And Arafah: meaning the day of Arafah, because the sunna has come for that. And obligatory for the deceased due to his statement: 'For the Muslim upon the Muslim are six rights: if he invites him, he should respond; if he is sick, he should visit him; if he dies, he should attend him; if he meets him, he should greet him; if he seeks his advice, he should advise him; if he sneezes, he should say yarhamuk Allah.' So his saying 'if he dies, he should attend him' indicates ghusl and everything related to preparing the deceased. And it was said: ghusl of the deceased is a strongly recommended sunnah. And in al-Wafi, ghusl after death is fard. (Fath, Miskeen)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings on ghusl (obligatory bath) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins with the issue of a woman's braided hair: if water reaches the roots, she need not undo her braids, based on the hadith of Umm Salama and to avoid hardship. Then it addresses the causes that necessitate ghusl: (1) Emission of maniy (semen) that exits with gushing flow (dafaq) and pleasure (shahwa). This is the Hanafi position; without dafaq and shahwa, ghusl is still obligatory, but they attach it to pleasure based on the hadith of Umm Salama linking ghusl to pleasure. The Shafi'i school holds that any emission of maniy necessitates ghusl, but the Hanafis rebut by specifying the hadith 'Water is from water' to emission with shahwa. (2) Meeting of the circumcised parts (glans entering the vagina or anus) even without ejaculation, based on the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory.' There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the anus: Abu Hanifa does not consider mere insertion into the anus sufficient for ghusl without emission, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) do, by qiyas on the front and because the hadd (for sodomy) is more severe.

The passage then covers ghusl due to hayd (menses) and nifas (postpartum bleeding) after they cease. It clarifies that madhi (prostatic fluid) and wadi (thick discharge) do not require ghusl, contradicting some views. Wet dreams without wetness also do not require ghusl. Various scenarios of finding wetness upon waking are detailed, including the distinction between maniy and madhi, and the ruling if both a man and woman find maniy on the bedding.

Finally, it lists recommended (sunnah) ghusl: for Friday, the two Eids, for ihram, and on the day of Arafah. Ghusl for the deceased is considered obligatory (fard) by some, or sunnah mu'akkadah by others; the text presents the view that it is obligatory based on the hadith of the six rights. The passage thus lays out the complete fiqh of ghusl according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual blood; upon its cessation, ghusl is obligatory.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding; requires ghusl upon cessation.
مذي (madhi): Prostatic fluid emitted during foreplay; does not require ghusl.
ودي (wadi): Thick white discharge that follows urine; does not require ghusl.
احتلام (ihtilam): Wet dream; ghusl is required only if fluid is emitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man wakes up, finds wetness in his urethra, and does not remember a dream. His private part was limp before sleep. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) He must perform ghusl because the wetness is likely maniy.
B) He does not need ghusl because the wetness might be madhi.
C) He must perform ghusl only if his private part was erect.
D) He should perform ghusl out of precaution.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is obligatory after hayd/nifas and upon certain emission of maniy; madhi and wadi require only wudu.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
7 min
Recommended Ghusl: Friday, Eid, Ihram, Arafah, and Ghusl for the Deceased
Lists recommended ghusl and discusses the ruling on ghusl for the deceased.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the occasions for which ghusl is recommended (sunnah) and the dispute regarding its obligation for the deceased.

Core Idea
Ghusl on Friday, Eid, Ihram, and Arafah is sunnah; ghusl of the deceased is either fard or sunnah mu'akkadah by different views.

This lesson enumerates the recommended (sunnah) ghusl occasions: Friday, the two Eids, entering ihram for Hajj/Umrah, and the day of Arafah. It also discusses the ghusl for the deceased, noting the difference of opinion between those who consider it fard (obligatory) and those who consider it sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). The text presents the evidence and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
List the four sunnah ghusls
From the passage: (1) Ghusl for Friday, (2) for the two Eids, (3) for ihram, (4) on the day of Arafah. Note that some consider these mustahabb (recommended).
These are confirmed by sunnah practices of the Prophet.
2
Examine the dispute on Friday ghusl
Malik considered it wajib; the Zahiris also said wajib. The Hanafi response: the hadith 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory' is abrogated or means 'stressed.'
The Hanafi school holds it as sunnah, not wajib.
3
Analyse the ruling for ghusl of the deceased
The text cites the hadith of the six rights: '... if he dies, he should attend him,' which includes ghusl. Some say it is fard; the text mentions a view that it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The preferred view in the Hanafi school is that it is fard kifayah.

كتاب الطهارة

المعاني الموجبة للغسل

ولا تنقض ضفيرة إن بل أصلها. (البحر الرائق: ۱۲۰/۱)] أي لو بلت المرأة في الاغتسال أصل شعرها لم يجب عليها نقض ضفيرتها، ولا يجب عليها بل ذوائبها وهو الصحيح، وقيد بقوله: إن بل أصلها؛ لأنه إن لم يبل أصلها وجب النقض عليها، فذكر المرأة؛ لأن الرجل إذا ضفر شعر رأسه كالعلوي والتركي يجب إيصال الماء إلى أثناء شعر رأسه احتياطاً، وإن وصل الماء إلى ما تحتها؛ لأن النص في المرأة؛ لقوله للأم سلمة حين قالت: يا رسول الله ! إني امرأة أضفر رأسي، أفأنقضها إذا اغتسلت؟ قال: "يكفيك إذا بلغ الماء أصول شعرك" وللحرج في حقها. (مسكين، مستخلص) وفرض عند مني إلخ أي فرض الغسل مع نزول مني ذي دفق أي دفوق ولذة، فالخروج بدون الدفق والشهوة يوجب الغسل عندنا خلافاً للشافعي، له قوله عليه: "الماء الماء" يعني وجوب الاغتسال بإنزال المني، ولنا: ما من روت أم سلمة أنها سألت النبي عن المرأة ترى في منامها مثل ما يرى الرجل، فقال عليه: "أتحد بذلك لذة" فقالت: نعم، فقال: "فلتغتسل" علق الاغتسال باللذة وحديث الشافعي محمول على الإنزال بشهوة، وإنما حملنا الحديث على الخروج بشهوة؛ لأنه عام لا يمكن إجراؤه على العموم؛ لأنه يتناول المذي والودي والمني بشهوة وغير شهوة، والمني يعتبر انفصاله بالشهوة هو المراد بالإجماع. ذي دفق يقال: دفق الماء دفقا، صبّه صبا فيه دفع شدة. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٥/١] عند انفصاله متعلق بقوله: دفق وشهوة ]، أي فرض الغسل عند خروج مني موصوف بالدفق والشهوة عند محله عند الطرفين، وأما عند أبي يوسف فيعتبر ظهوره على وجه الشهوة أيضاً كما انفصال المني عن . كما إذا اغتسل قبل أن يبول، ثم سال عنه بقية المني يجب الغسل عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. (مسكين) وتواري إلخ التواري الغيبوبة والحشفة ما فوق الختان، أي موضع القطع من الذكر والأنثى، يعني فرض الغسل عند تغيب الحشفة أو قدرها من مقطوعه، وقوله : "في قبل أو دبر" أي المتحققين من آدمي، حتى لو كان بهيمة أو ميتة لا يجب الغسل بدون الإنزال ؛ لقصور الداعي فيهما، والوجوب لقوله عليه: "إذا التقى الختانان وتوارت الحشفة وجب الغسل، أنزل أو لم ينزل"؛ ولأنه سبب الإنزال، فيقام سبب الظاهر مقامه كنوم المضطجع، وإنما قيل بالقبل والدبر ؛ لأنه لو جامع امرأته في ما دونهما كالسرة والفخذ وتوارت الحشفة لم يجب الغسل ما لم ينزل، وقوله: "عليهما" أي على الفاعل والمفعول، أي الرجل والمرأة المكلفين، والدليل على وجوب الغسل بمجرد تغيب الحشفة في القبل وإن لم ينزل حديث أبي هريرة أنه عليه قال: "إذا جلس بين شعبها الأربع ثم جهدها فقد وجب الغسل"، وصح عن عائشة لها أنها قالت: "إذا جاوز الختان الختان وجب الغسل"، وأما في صورة الدبر فعند أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ لأنه لما وجب الحد الذي يحتاط في تركه فلأن يجب الغسل أولى، وأما عند أبي حنيفة فلأن الاحتياط في الحد تركه؛ لأنه من العقوبات، وفي إيجاب الغسل احتياط؛ لأنه من العبادات. (فتح، مسكين وغيره) حشفة: هي ما فوق الختان ولو بحائل توجد معه الحرارة على الأصح. (ط) عليهما أي الفاعل والمفعول لو مكلفين، فلو أحدهما مكلفا فعليه فقط وإن لم ينزل . (ط) وحيض ونفاس أي فرض الغسل عند انقطاع حيض ونفاس. (ط) لا مذي إلخ عطف على "منى"، أي لا يغسل عند خروج مذي وهو الذي يخرج عند الملاعبة ولا ودي، ولا عند احتلام، وهو ما يرى النائم من الجماع بلا بلل مطلقا، سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة، وقال محمد: على المرأة الغسل احتياطاً إذا التذت لذة الإنزال، أما من استيقظ فوجد على فراشه أو فخذه بللاً وهو يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه مني أو شك فعليه الغسل، أما إذا لم يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه مني أو شك فكذلك، وإن تيقن أنه مذي فلا غسل عليه، وإذا استيقظ فوجد في إحليله بللاً ولم يتذكر حلماً إن كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا غسل عليه، وإن كان ساكناً فعليه الغسل، هذا إذا نام قائما أو قاعدا، أما إذا نام مضطجعاً وتيقن أنه مني فعليه الغسل، فهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وإن استيقظ الرجل والمرأة فوجدا منياً على الفراش، وكل واحد منهما ينكر الاحتلام وجب عليهما الغسل، وقال بعضهم: إن كان المني طويلاً أو أبيض فعلى الرجل، وإن كان مدوراً أو أصفر فعلى المرأة. (مسكين) وودي هو بول غليظ أبيض يتعقب الرقيق منه. (ط) وسن للجمعة إلخ : أي سن الغسل لأجل الجمعة وغيرها، وقيل: هذه الأربعة مستحبة، وسمى محمد الغسل في الجمعة حسناً في "الأصل"، وقال مالك: هو واجب وقال بعض الشارحين: إنه غير صحيح؛ فإنه لم يقل بالوجوب إلا أهل الظاهر، ودليلهم قوله عليه: "غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم"، والجواب أنه منسوخ أو هو من باب انتهاء الحكم لانتهاء العلة؛ لأن الناس كانوا يلبسون الصوف وكان مسجدهم ضيقاً، فخرج عليها في يوم حار وعرق الناس في ذلك الصوف حتى ظهرت منه رياح ثم كثر الخير ولبسوا غير الصوف ووسع مسجدهم، أو المراد بالواجب الثابت. (مسكين) والإحرام: أي عند إحرام الحج والعمرة. (ط) وعرفة: أي يوم عرفة؛ لورود السنة بذلك. ووجب للميت لقوله عليه: "للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق: إذا دعاه أن يجيبه، وإذا مرض أن يعوده، وإذا مات أن يحضره، وإذا لقيه أن يسلم عليه، وإذا استنصحه أن ينصحه، وإذا عطس أن يشمته"، فقوله: إذا مات أن يحضره يدل على الغسل وغيره من كل ما تعلق بتجهيز الميت، وقيل: غسل الميت سنة مؤكدة، وفي "الوافي" الغسل بعد الموت فرض. (فتح، مسكين) يوم
Book of Purification. The meanings that necessitate ghusl. And she does not undo her braid if its root becomes wet. (From al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/120) Meaning: If a woman wets the root of her hair while bathing, she is not obligated to undo her braid, and she is not obligated to wet the locks; this is the correct view. It is restricted by his saying 'if its root becomes wet' because if its root does not become wet, she must undo it. The mention of the woman is because if a man braids his hair like an Alawi or Turk, he must deliver water to the inside of his hair as a precaution, even if water reaches beneath it, because the text is for the woman, due to his statement to Umm Salama when she said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who braids my hair; should I undo it when I bathe?' He said, 'It suffices you if water reaches the roots of your hair' and due to hardship for her. (Miskeen, Mustakhlas) And obligatory upon maniy etc. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory with the descent of maniy that has dafaq (gushing) and shahwa (pleasure). So emission without dafaq and shahwa necessitates ghusl according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He has his statement: 'Water is from water' meaning obligation of ghusl by the emission of maniy. And we have what Umm Salama narrated that she asked the Prophet about a woman who sees in her dream what a man sees. He said, 'Do you experience pleasure from that?' She said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Then let her bathe.' He attached ghusl to pleasure. And the hadith of al-Shafi'i is interpreted as emission with shahwa. We interpreted the hadith as emission with shahwa because it is general and cannot be applied generally because it includes madhi, wadi, and maniy with and without shahwa, and maniy whose separation is with shahwa is intended by consensus. 'Dafaq' is said: he poured water pouring it, pouring it with force. (al-Bahr al-Raiq: 1/125) 'At its separation' is attached to his saying 'dafaq and shahwa'. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory at the emanation of maniy described with gushing and shahwa at its place according to both sides. As for Abu Yusuf, he considers its appearance with shahwa as well as the separation of maniy? Just as if he bathed before urinating, then the remainder of maniy flowed, ghusl is obligatory according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Hanifa. (Miskeen) And concealment etc. al-Tawari is disappearance, and al-Hashafah is what is above the circumcision, i.e., the place of cutting from the male and female. Meaning: Ghusl is obligatory upon concealment of the glans or its equivalent from one whose glans is cut off, and his saying 'in the front or back' means actual ones from a human. Even if it were an animal or a corpse, ghusl is not obligatory without emission because of lack of desire. And obligation is due to his statement: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans becomes concealed, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' And because it is a cause of emission, so the apparent cause is established in its place like the sleep of one lying on his side. And it was said only with front and back because if he had intercourse with his wife in other than them, like the navel and thigh, and the glans became concealed, ghusl is not obligatory unless he ejaculates. And his saying 'upon both' means upon the doer and the recipient, i.e., the man and the woman who are legally responsible. And the evidence for the obligation of ghusl by mere concealment of the glans in the front even if he does not ejaculate is the hadith of Abu Hurayra that he said: 'When he sits between her four branches and then exerts himself, ghusl becomes obligatory.' And it is authentic from Aisha that she said: 'When the circumcision passes the circumcision, ghusl becomes obligatory.' As for the case of the back, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because when the hadd becomes obligatory, which one is cautious in avoiding, so the obligation of ghusl is more appropriate. And according to Abu Hanifa, caution in the hadd is its avoidance because it is a punishment, and in obligating ghusl is caution because it is an act of worship. (Fath, Miskeen, etc.) al-Hashafah: It is what is above the circumcision even with a barrier that is accompanied by heat according to the correct view. (T) 'upon both' means the doer and recipient if they are legally responsible; if one of them is legally responsible, then only upon him even if he does not ejaculate. (T) And hayd and nifas: meaning ghusl is obligatory at the cessation of hayd and nifas. (T) Not madhi etc. is conjuncted to 'maniy', meaning: ghusl is not required upon emission of madhi, which is emitted during foreplay, nor wadi, nor upon a wet dream, which is what a sleeper sees of intercourse without any wetness, whether man or woman. And Muhammad said: upon the woman, ghusl is obligatory as a precaution if she experiences the pleasure of ejaculation. As for one who wakes up and finds wetness on his bedding or thigh and he remembers a wet dream and is certain it is maniy or is in doubt, he must perform ghusl. As for if he does not remember a wet dream and is certain it is maniy or is in doubt, likewise. And if he is certain it is madhi, then no ghusl upon him. And if he wakes up and finds wetness in his urethra and does not remember a dream, if his private part was erect before sleep, no ghusl upon him; if it was limp, then ghusl is upon him. This is if he slept standing or sitting. As for if he slept lying down and is certain it is maniy, then ghusl is upon him. This issue occurs frequently and people are negligent of it. And if a man and woman wake up and find maniy on the bedding, and each of them denies a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory upon both. And some said: if the maniy is long or white, then upon the man; if it is round or yellow, then upon the woman. (Miskeen) And wadi is thick white urine that follows the thin urine. (T) And sunnah for Friday etc.: meaning: ghusl for Friday and others is sunnah. And it was said: these four are recommended. Muhammad called ghusl on Friday 'good' in al-Asl. Malik said it is obligatory. And some commentators said this is incorrect; only the Zahiris said it is obligatory. Their evidence is his statement: 'Ghusl on Friday is obligatory upon every pubescent person.' The answer is that it is abrogated or it is from the category of termination of ruling due to termination of cause, because the people used to wear wool and their mosque was narrow, so he went out on a hot day and the people sweated in that wool until odors appeared from it. Then prosperity increased and they wore other than wool and their mosque was expanded. Or what is meant by 'obligatory' is established. (Miskeen) And al-Ihram: meaning when entering ihram for hajj and umra. (T) And Arafah: meaning the day of Arafah, because the sunna has come for that. And obligatory for the deceased due to his statement: 'For the Muslim upon the Muslim are six rights: if he invites him, he should respond; if he is sick, he should visit him; if he dies, he should attend him; if he meets him, he should greet him; if he seeks his advice, he should advise him; if he sneezes, he should say yarhamuk Allah.' So his saying 'if he dies, he should attend him' indicates ghusl and everything related to preparing the deceased. And it was said: ghusl of the deceased is a strongly recommended sunnah. And in al-Wafi, ghusl after death is fard. (Fath, Miskeen)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings on ghusl (obligatory bath) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins with the issue of a woman's braided hair: if water reaches the roots, she need not undo her braids, based on the hadith of Umm Salama and to avoid hardship. Then it addresses the causes that necessitate ghusl: (1) Emission of maniy (semen) that exits with gushing flow (dafaq) and pleasure (shahwa). This is the Hanafi position; without dafaq and shahwa, ghusl is still obligatory, but they attach it to pleasure based on the hadith of Umm Salama linking ghusl to pleasure. The Shafi'i school holds that any emission of maniy necessitates ghusl, but the Hanafis rebut by specifying the hadith 'Water is from water' to emission with shahwa. (2) Meeting of the circumcised parts (glans entering the vagina or anus) even without ejaculation, based on the hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory.' There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the anus: Abu Hanifa does not consider mere insertion into the anus sufficient for ghusl without emission, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) do, by qiyas on the front and because the hadd (for sodomy) is more severe.

The passage then covers ghusl due to hayd (menses) and nifas (postpartum bleeding) after they cease. It clarifies that madhi (prostatic fluid) and wadi (thick discharge) do not require ghusl, contradicting some views. Wet dreams without wetness also do not require ghusl. Various scenarios of finding wetness upon waking are detailed, including the distinction between maniy and madhi, and the ruling if both a man and woman find maniy on the bedding.

Finally, it lists recommended (sunnah) ghusl: for Friday, the two Eids, for ihram, and on the day of Arafah. Ghusl for the deceased is considered obligatory (fard) by some, or sunnah mu'akkadah by others; the text presents the view that it is obligatory based on the hadith of the six rights. The passage thus lays out the complete fiqh of ghusl according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice; omission is not sinful but reward is lost.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; in the context of deceased, fard kifayah.
إحرام (ihram): Sacred state for Hajj/Umrah; ghusl before entering ihram is sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the ruling for ghusl on the day of 'Arafah?
A) Fard (obligatory) for all pilgrims.
B) Sunnah (recommended) because the sunna has come for it.
C) Mustahabb only for the imam.
D) Not required at all.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is sunnah on Friday, Eid, ihram, and Arafah; ghusl for the deceased is fard kifayah.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Obligatory Ghusl: Causes and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Anal Intercourse
Listing obligatory causes and resolving an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory causes of ghusl and explain why Abu Hanifa differed from the Sahibayn regarding anal intercourse.

Core Idea
Insertion of the hashafah into either passage triggers ghusl, but Abu Hanifa held that anal intercourse does not necessitate it.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists the causes that make ghusl obligatory: insertion of the glans, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and seminal emission. The most debated is anal intercourse, where Abu Hanifa's position diverges from his two major disciples. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the qiyas argument, and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory causes
Read the first line of the matn. Ghusl becomes obligatory due to: (1) hashafah entering the front or back passage, (2) menstruation, (3) postpartum bleeding. Also note that madhi and wadi do not require ghusl, nor does a wet dream without fluid.
The matn lists these as causes of janabah.
2
Define 'hashafah'
The commentary defines hashafah as the part above the circumcision, even with a barrier, as long as heat is felt (al-asahh). This applies to both partners if both are legally responsible.
The same definition applies for both front and back.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on anal intercourse
Abu Hanifa held that ghusl is not obligatory for anal intercourse, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) held it is obligatory. The text presents both positions and their proofs.
The dispute is on the secondary cause: entry into the back passage.
4
Follow the qiyas of the Sahibayn
They argued: since hadd (punishment for sodomy) is obligatory and people are cautious to avoid it, then ghusl, which is a lighter act of worship, should be even more obligatory. This is qiyas from the greater to the lesser (awlawi).
Qiyas awlawi: if a heavier thing is obligatory, the lighter is also.
5
Understand Abu Hanifa's rebuttal and the tarjih
Abu Hanifa replied: caution regarding hadd is to avoid it (since it is a punishment), while caution regarding ghusl is to perform it (since it is worship). The analogy fails because the direction of caution is opposite. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, making ghusl obligatory.
The text later says 'a'ni 'alayhi al-fatwa' implicitly through the commentary's approval.

الأسباب الموجبة للغسل: حشفة في قبل أو دبرٍ عليهما، وحيض ونفاس لا مذي وودي، واحتلام بلا بلل، نأي لا عند احتلام وسُن للجمعة والعيدين والإحرام وعرفة ووجب للميت، أي الغسل أي لصلاتها على المسلمين أي الغسل للميت = وأما في صورة الدبر فعند أبي يوسف ومحمد؛ لأنه لما وجب الحد الذي يحتاط في تركه فلأن يجب الغسل أولى، وأما عند أبي حنيفة فلأن الاحتياط في الحد تركه؛ لأنه من العقوبات، وفي إيجاب الغسل احتياط؛ لأنه من العبادات. (فتح، مسكين وغيره) حشفة: هي ما فوق الختان ولو بحائل توجد معه الحرارة على الأصح. (ط) عليهما أي الفاعل والمفعول لو مكلفين، فلو أحدهما مكلفا فعليه فقط وإن لم ينزل . (ط) وحيض ونفاس أي فرض الغسل عند انقطاع حيض ونفاس. (ط) لا مذي إلخ عطف على "منى"، أي لا يغسل عند خروج مذي وهو الذي يخرج عند الملاعبة] ولا ودي، ولا عند احتلام، وهو ما يرى النائم من الجماع بلا بلل مطلقا، سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة، وقال محمد: على المرأة الغسل احتياطاً إذا التذت لذة الإنزال، أما من استيقظ فوجد على فراشه أو فخذه بللاً وهو يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أو مذي أو شك فعليه الغسل، أما إذا لم يتذكر الاحتلام وتيقن أنه أو شك فكذلك، وإن تيقن أنه مذي فلا غسل عليه، وإذا استيقظ فوجد في إحليله بللاً ولم يتذكر حلماً إن كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا غسل عليه، وإن كان ساكناً فعليه الغسل، هذا إذا نام قائما أو قاعدا، أما إذا نام وتيقن أنه فعليه الغسل، فهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وإن استيقظ الرجل والمرأة فوجدا منياً على الفراش، وكل واحد منهما ينكر الاحتلام وجب عليهما الغسل، وقال بعضهم: إن كان المني طويلاً أو أبيض فعلى الرجل، وإن كان مدوراً أو أصفر فعلى المرأة. (مسكين وودي هو بول غليظ أبيض يتعقب الرقيق منه. (ط) وسن للجمعة إلخ : أي سن الغسل لأجل الجمعة وغيرها، وقيل: هذه الأربعة مستحبة، وسمى محمد الغسل في الجمعة حسناً في "الأصل"، وقال مالك: هو واجب وقال بعض الشارحين: إنه غير صحيح؛ فإنه لم يقل بالوجوب إلا أهل الظاهر، ودليلهم قوله عليه: "غسل يوم الجمعة واجب على كل محتلم"، والجواب أنه منسوخ أو هو من باب انتهاء الحكم لانتهاء العلة؛ لأن الناس كانوا يلبسون الصوف وكان مسجدهم . ضيقاً، فخرج عليها في يوم حار وعرق الناس في ذلك الصوف حتى ظهرت منه رياح ثم كثر الخير ولبسوا غير الصوف ووسع مسجدهم، أو المراد بالواجب الثابت. (مسكين) والإحرام: أي عند إحرام الحج والعمرة. (ط) وعرفة: أي يوم عرفة؛ لورود السنة بذلك. ووجب للميت لقوله علي: "للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق: إذا دعاه أن يجيبه، وإذا مرض أن يعوده، وإذا مات أن يحضره، وإذا لقيه أن يسلم عليه، وإذا استنصحه أن ينصحه، وإذا عطس أن يشمته، فقوله: إذا" مات أن يحضره" يدل على الغسل وغيره من كل ما تعلق بتجهيز الميت، وقيل: غسل الميت سنة مؤكدة، وفي "الوافي" الغسل بعد الموت فرض. (فتح، مسكين)

كتاب الطهارة ولمن أسلم إلخ أي وجب الغسل إذا أجنب الكافر ثم أسلم، وقول من قال بأن الجنابة في حق الكافر لا توجب الاغتسال بعد الإسلام؛ لأن الكفار غير مخاطبين بالشرائع، أي العبادات غير سديد؛ لأنهم وإن كانوا غير مخاطبين فالاغتسال لا يجب بالجنابة حتى يقال إنه وقت وجوب الاغتسال غير مخاطب، وإنما وجوبه بإرادة الصلاة ونحوها، وهو عند تلك الإرادة جنب مسلم، وإن أسلم ولم يكن جنباً يستحب له الغسل؛ لقوله عليه: "من جاء يريد الإسلام إن كان جنباً فليغتسل وإلا فلا". (مسكين وغيره)
The causes that make ghusl obligatory: the circumcised part (glans) entering the front or back passage of either partner, menstruation and postpartum bleeding, not madhi and wadi, and a wet dream without fluid, except that ghusl is not required for a wet dream without emission. Ghusl is sunnah for Friday, the two Eids, entering ihram, and the day of 'Arafah, and it is obligatory for the deceased, meaning ghusl for the deceased is obligatory upon the Muslims. As for the case of the back passage: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because when the hadd punishment becomes obligatory (due to anal intercourse), which one is cautious in abandoning, then ghusl is even more obligatory. According to Abu Hanifa, caution in the hadd is to abandon it because it is a punishment, whereas in making ghusl obligatory, caution is to perform it because it is an act of worship. (Fath, Miskin etc.) Al-hashafah: what is above the circumcision, even with a barrier such that heat is felt, according to the most correct view. 'Alayhima' refers to both the active and passive partner if both are legally responsible; if only one is responsible, ghusl is only on that one even without emission. Menstruation and postpartum: ghusl becomes obligatory at their cessation. 'La madhi ila' etc. is connected to 'maniy', meaning ghusl is not performed for the emission of madhi, which is emitted during play, nor for wadi, nor for a wet dream without any fluid absolutely, whether the person is male or female. Muhammad said: the woman must perform ghusl as a precaution if she experienced the pleasure of orgasm. As for one who wakes up and finds wetness on his bedding or thigh while remembering a wet dream and is certain it is semen or madhi or is unsure, then ghusl is obligatory. If he does not remember a wet dream and is certain it is semen or unsure, likewise. If he is certain it is madhi, no ghusl. If he wakes up and finds wetness on his penis and does not remember a dream, if his organ was erect before sleep, no ghusl; if it was flaccid, ghusl is obligatory. This is if he slept sitting or standing. If he slept lying down and is certain it is semen, ghusl is obligatory. This issue is common and people are heedless of it. If a man and woman wake up and find semen on the bed and each denies a wet dream, ghusl is obligatory on both. Some said: if the semen is long and white, it is from the man; if round and yellow, from the woman. (Miskin) Wadi is thick white urine that follows the dilute one. Ghusl is sunnah for Friday etc.: meaning ghusl for Friday and others is sunnah. It is said that these four are recommended. Muhammad called ghusl on Friday 'hasan' in al-Asl. Malik said it is obligatory. Some commentators said this is incorrect because only the Zahiris held it obligatory. Their evidence is the hadith: 'Ghusl on Friday is wajib upon every adult male.' The response is that it is abrogated, or it is a matter of the ruling ending due to the end of the cause because people used to wear wool and their mosque was narrow. The Prophet came out on a hot day and people sweated in that wool until odors appeared. Then prosperity increased and they wore other than wool and the mosque was expanded. Or what is meant by 'wajib' is confirmed (thabit). (Miskin) Al-ihram: meaning at the time of entering ihram for Hajj and Umrah. 'Arafah: meaning the day of 'Arafah, because the sunnah has come with that. And ghusl is obligatory for the deceased due to his saying: 'A Muslim has six rights over another Muslim: when he invites him, he should respond; when he is sick, he should visit him; when he dies, he should attend his funeral; when he meets him, he should greet him; when he seeks advice, he should advise him; when he sneezes, he should say yarhamukallah.' So his saying 'when he dies, he should attend' indicates ghusl and everything related to preparing the deceased. It is said that ghusl of the deceased is a stressed sunnah, and in al-Wafi, ghusl after death is fard. (Fath, Miskin) Kitab al-Taharah: 'And for the one who becomes Muslim': meaning ghusl becomes obligatory if an unbeliever becomes junub and then accepts Islam. The statement of those who say that janabah in the case of an unbeliever does not necessitate ghusl after Islam because unbelievers are not addressed by the laws is unsound. Because even if they are not addressed, ghusl is not obligatory due to janabah so that it could be said that at the time of obligation he is not addressed. Rather its obligation is when he intends prayer and the like, and at that time he is a junub Muslim. If he becomes Muslim and is not junub, ghusl is recommended for him due to his saying: 'Whoever comes wanting Islam, if he is junub let him perform ghusl, otherwise not.' (Miskin etc.)
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the causes that make ghusl obligatory or recommended in the Hanafi school. The matn lists: insertion of the glans (hashafah) into the front or back passage, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding as obligatory causes; madhi and wadi do not require ghusl; a wet dream without fluid does not require ghusl. The commentary expands on each. For anal intercourse, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that since hadd punishment is obligatory (for sodomy) and one is cautious in abandoning it, ghusl is even more obligatory. Abu Hanifa argues that caution regarding hadd is to avoid it (since it is a punishment), while caution regarding ghusl is to perform it (since it is worship); hence ghusl is not obligatory for anal intercourse in his view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn. The passage also details rulings on waking up with wetness. For Friday ghusl, the text notes a dispute with Malik who considered it wajib. The Hanafi response is that the hadith 'ghusl yawm al-jumu'ah wajib' is either abrogated or the wajib meant is 'thabit' (confirmed) not legally obligatory. The passage concludes with ghusl for the deceased (obligatory on Muslims as a fard kifayah) and for a new Muslim (obligatory if junub, recommended otherwise).

Key Terms
حشفة (hashafah): The part of the male organ above the circumcision (glans); the point of insertion that triggers ghusl.
مذي (madhy): A thin fluid that exits during foreplay or arousal; does not necessitate ghusl but requires wudu.
ودي (wady): Thick white urine that follows the dilute urine; does not necessitate ghusl.
احتلام (ihtilam): A wet dream without the emission of fluid; does not necessitate ghusl according to the matn, but the commentary discusses nuances.
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, caused by sexual intercourse or emission of semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position regarding ghusl for anal intercourse in the Hanafi school?
A) Ghusl is not obligatory (Abu Hanifa's view).
B) Ghusl is obligatory (Sahibayn's view).
C) Ghusl is recommended but not obligatory.
D) Ghusl is only required if fluid is emitted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that ghusl is obligatory for both front and back insertion of the hashafah, following the Sahibayn's qiyas from hadd.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
7 min
Recommended Ghusl: Friday, Eids, Ihram, Arafah, and the Friday Ghusl Dispute
Listing recommended ghusl and resolving an inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four recommended occasions for ghusl and explain the Hanafi position in the dispute over whether Friday ghusl is wajib.

Core Idea
Friday ghusl is sunnah in the Hanafi school, not wajib, despite the hadith's literal wording.

After listing the obligatory causes, the matn states that ghusl is sunnah for Friday, the two Eids, entering ihram, and standing at Arafah. The commentary notes a significant dispute: Imam Malik and the Zahiris consider Friday ghusl wajib based on a hadith. This lesson examines the Hanafi response, including the arguments of abrogation and change of circumstance, and concludes with the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
List the four recommended occasions
The matn says: 'Wa sunna lil-jumu'ah wal-'idayn wal-ihram wa 'Arafah.' These are Friday, the two Eids, entering ihram, and the day of Arafah.
Some narrations add the night of Arafah, but the matn specifies day.
2
Note Muhammad's description of Friday ghusl
Imam Muhammad called Friday ghusl 'hasan' (good) in al-Asl, indicating it is not obligatory but recommended.
This is weaker than sunnah mu'akkadah according to some.
3
Identify the dispute with Malik and the Zahiris
Malik and the Zahiris considered Friday ghusl wajib. Their evidence is the hadith: 'Ghusl yawm al-jumu'ah wajib 'ala kull muhtalim.'
The Zahiris are the only group that literally holds it wajib; Malik's view is also mentioned.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond with two arguments: (1) The hadith is abrogated (mansukh) because the ruling changed when the mosque was expanded and people wore lighter clothes. (2) The word 'wajib' is interpreted as 'thabit' (confirmed) meaning sunnah mu'akkadah, not legally obligatory.
The change of circumstance ('illah) ended, so the ruling ended.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that Friday ghusl is sunnah, not wajib. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The text also mentions ghusl for the deceased (obligatory) and for a new Muslim (obligatory if junub, recommended otherwise).

Commentary

Abu Hanifa argues that caution regarding hadd is to avoid it (since it is a punishment), while caution regarding ghusl is to perform it (since it is worship); hence ghusl is not obligatory for anal intercourse in his view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn. The passage also details rulings on waking up with wetness. For Friday ghusl, the text notes a dispute with Malik who considered it wajib. The Hanafi response is that the hadith 'ghusl yawm al-jumu'ah wajib' is either abrogated or the wajib meant is 'thabit' (confirmed) not legally obligatory. The passage concludes with ghusl for the deceased (obligatory on Muslims as a fard kifayah) and for a new Muslim (obligatory if junub, recommended otherwise).

Key Terms
غسل الجمعة (ghusl al-jumu'ah): The ritual bath performed for Friday prayer; in the Hanafi school it is sunnah, not wajib.
محتلم (muhtalim): An adult male who has reached puberty (literally one who has wet dreams).
ثابت (thabit): Confirmed or established; in the context, an interpretation of 'wajib' as meaning a confirmed sunnah rather than legally obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's ruling on ghusl for Friday?
A) Wajib (obligatory).
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (recommended).
C) Mubah (permissible).
D) Makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that Friday ghusl is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation, based on abrogation or reinterpretation of the hadith.

Taharah — Purification

Permissible Water for Wudu in Hanafi Fiqh
Explains types of water for wudu and effect of pure mixtures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for water to be valid for wudu and apply the Hanafi rule that change by a pure substance does not invalidate unless the water loses its name.

Core Idea
Water remains purifying for wudu unless a pure substance overwhelms it and it is no longer called 'water'.

In this passage, the author sets out which waters are valid for wudu. The key principle is that absolute water (ma' mutlaq) is the default purifier. Even if a pure substance changes its color, taste, or smell, the water remains valid as long as it is still called 'water'. However, if the change is so extreme that it becomes known as 'leaf-water' or 'saffron-water', it loses its absolute status. The passage also addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i on this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The matn states that rainwater, spring water, and sea water are permissible for wudu. The commentary clarifies that any absolute water (including river, well, snow, hail) is valid.
The core principle: absolute water is always purifying unless it becomes muqayyad.
2
Apply the condition of change by pure substances
Even if a pure substance changes one of the water's properties (color, taste, smell) or it becomes foul from stagnation, it remains valid. The hadith 'Water is purifying; nothing pure makes it impure...' supports this.
Change by a pure substance does not transform the water into muqayyad unless the change is extreme (dominant by parts).
3
Distinguish between valid change and invalid overwhelming
If the water is so mixed with a pure substance that it is no longer called 'water' (e.g., broth, bean water, pressed fruit juice), wudu is invalid. However, water that has only changed color due to leaves but still retains the name 'water' remains valid.
Dominance is determined by parts, not by color or smell alone.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that water mixed with saffron becomes muqayyad and invalid for wudu. The Hanafi response: the addition is for identification, not restriction, and the mixture must be dominant in parts, not just color.
The practical difference: Hanafis allow wudu with saffron-water if it is still called 'water'; Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مستخلص) :والعين وكذا النهر والبئر والثلج والبرد. (ط) أحد أوصافه أو كلها وهي اللون والطعم والرائحة. (ط) بالمكث بطول الإقامة في موضعه. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸/۱] لا بماء إلخ: أي لا يجوز الوضوء بماء تغير لونه بكثرة الأوراق الواقعة فيه، لكن يجوز شربه وغسل الأشياء به؛ لأنه طاهر، وأما عدم جواز التوضي به؛ لأنه غلب عليه الأوراق وصار مقيدا كماء الباقلى، وعلله في النهر الفائق [٧٢/١] بزوال اسم الماء عنه السخنه. (مستخلص) تغيّر بأن خرج عن رقته وسيلانه. (ط) أو بالطبخ إلخ أي لا يتوضأ بماء تغير بسبب الطبخ بخلط طاهر كالمرق والباقلى؛ لأنه لم يبق ماء مطلقا فلم يتناوله النص، وكذا الحكم في ماء اعتصر من شجر أو ثمر ؛ لأنه ليس بماء مطلق، وفي ذكر العصر إشارة إلى أن ما يخرج من كماء يسيل من الكرم يجوز به الوضوء، وهو قول بعض المشايخ، وقوله: "أو غلب عليه غيره" أي لا يجوز التوضي بماء غلب عليه غير الماء من جهة الأجزاء، وهو احتراز عن الغلبة لونا وهو قول محمد؛ لزوال = الشجر بلا عصر
And one performs wudu with rainwater, spring water, and sea water, even if a pure thing changes one of its properties or it becomes foul due to stagnation, for the one intending prayer, even if the change is from something not of the same genus as earth, meaning its smell changes. Not with water that has changed due to an abundance of leaves, or due to cooking, or that has been pressed from a tree or fruit, nor with water mixed with a pure substance like broth or broad beans, like rhubarb, like grapes. And he performs wudu etc.: when he finished explaining the two purifications, he mentioned what purifies, which is absolute water (al-ma' al-mutlaq): the one intending prayer performs wudu with these waters due to His saying: 'Wash your faces' (5:6), and the customary washing is with absolute water. Even if a pure thing changes one of its properties—meaning its color, taste, or smell—or it becomes foul from long stagnation, because it remains in the state of purity due to his saying: 'Water is purifying; nothing pure makes it impure except that which changes its color, taste, or smell.' And there is a dispute with al-Shafi'i, for he says: wudu is not permissible with saffron water and the like that are not from the genus of earth, because it is restricted water (muqayyad) called 'saffron water', unlike earth components, for water is never free of them usually. For us, the addition to saffron is like adding to a well or spring for identification, not for restriction. A small mixture is not considered; what matters is the dominant. Dominance is by parts, not by change of color. What is meant by 'what changes' in the hadith is something impure. (Mustakhlas) And the spring, as well as the river, well, snow, and hail. One of its properties or all: color, taste, smell. 'Bil-makth' means by long stay in its place. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:18) 'La bi ma' etc.: wudu is not permissible with water whose color has changed due to abundance of leaves falling into it, but it is permissible to drink it and wash things with it because it is pure. The reason it is not permissible for wudu is that leaves have overwhelmed it and it has become restricted (muqayyad) like bean water. Al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (1:72) explains it as the name of water having ceased from it. 'Taghayyara' means it left its fluidity and flow. 'Awt tabkh' etc.: wudu is not performed with water that changed due to cooking with a pure mixture like broth and beans because it is no longer absolute water, so the text does not cover it. Similarly, the ruling for water pressed from a tree or fruit, because it is not absolute water. The mention of pressing indicates that what comes out like the water that flows from the grapevine (without pressing) is permissible for wudu, according to some mashayikh. His saying 'or something else overwhelms it' means wudu is not permissible with water in which non-water has overwhelmed in terms of parts, which is a precaution against overwhelming in color. This is the view of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage explains the types of water permissible for wudu in the Hanafi school. The matn states that rainwater, spring water, and sea water are valid even if their properties change due to pure substances or stagnation. However, water that has changed due to an abundance of leaves, cooking, or pressing from trees/fruits is not valid. The commentary clarifies that 'absolute water' (ma' mutlaq) remains purifying even if its color, taste, or smell change due to a pure substance, as long as it is still called water. A dispute with Shafi'i is noted: Shafi'i holds that water mixed with saffron etc. becomes 'restricted' (muqayyad) and invalid for wudu. Hanafis respond that the addition is for identification, not restriction, and the mixture must be dominant by parts, not just color. The passage also distinguishes between water that is simply stagnant (still purifying) and water overwhelmed by pure substances (no longer absolute water). The example of leaves: if leaves are so many that the water is called 'leaf-water', wudu is invalid, but drinking is okay. Similarly, cooked water (like broth) or pressed fruit juice is not absolute water. However, water that naturally flows from grapevines (without pressing) is permissible according to some scholars. The relied-upon position is that absolute water must remain predominant by substance, not just appearance.

Key Terms
ماء مطلق (ma' mutlaq): Absolute, unrestricted water that is naturally occurring and suitable for wudu as long as it remains called 'water'.
ماء مقيد (ma' muqayyad): Restricted water that has been so dominated by a pure substance that it is no longer called 'water' (e.g., broth, juice). Not valid for wudu.
طهور (tahur): Legally pure and purifying in itself (used for wudu). This status applies to absolute water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because bad smell indicates impurity.
C) Only if it is still clear in color.
D) No, unless it is mixed with something pure.

Key Takeaway
Absolute water remains purifying for wudu unless it is so dominated by a pure substance that it is no longer called 'water'.

Ghusl for a Convert upon Entering Islam
States the ruling of ghusl for a convert, distinguishing janabah from non-janabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of ghusl for a convert, distinguish between janabah and non-janabah, and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Ghusl for a convert is wajib only if in janabah; otherwise it is sunnah.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for a person who embraces Islam. It addresses the common question of whether a convert must perform ghusl, and if so, under what conditions. The answer depends on whether the convert was in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) at the time of conversion. We will explore the textual evidence and the reasoning behind the school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon (ghusl for a convert) and what the hukm (legal ruling) is in two cases: in janabah and not in janabah.
The ruling is conditional on the convert's state of impurity.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited by the author—the hadith: 'Whoever comes wanting Islam, if he is junub let him perform ghusl, otherwise not.'
This hadith is the primary textual evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The conditional 'if... then' indicates that ghusl is required only when the condition (janabah) is met. The imperative 'فليغتسل' implies obligation (wujub). The exception 'وإلا فلا' shows that when not in janabah, ghusl is not obligatory, making it recommended.
The linguistic structure is key to the derivation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: some argue that since disbelievers are not addressed by the shari'ah, their janabah does not necessitate ghusl after Islam.
The Hanafi response refutes this by shifting the obligation to the time of intending prayer.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi). The hadith directly supports the distinction, and the reasoning that obligation arises at prayer intention is sound.
This is the established ruling in the school, with no major intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمن أسلم إلخ أي وجب الغسل إذا أجنب الكافر ثم أسلم، وقول من قال بأن الجنابة في حق الكافر لا توجب الاغتسال بعد الإسلام؛ لأن الكفار غير مخاطبين بالشرائع، أي العبادات غير سديد؛ لأنهم وإن كانوا غير مخاطبين فالاغتسال لا يجب بالجنابة حتى يقال إنه وقت وجوب الاغتسال غير مخاطب، وإنما وجوبه بإرادة الصلاة ونحوها، وهو عند تلك الإرادة جنب مسلم، وإن أسلم و لم يكن جنباً يستحب له الغسل؛ لقوله عليه: "من جاء يريد الإسلام إن كان جنباً فليغتسل وإلا فلا". (مسكين وغيره)
And for one who becomes Muslim, etc.: i.e., ghusl becomes obligatory if the disbeliever was in a state of janabah and then embraced Islam. The statement of those who say that janabah for a disbeliever does not necessitate ghusl after Islam because disbelievers are not addressed by the laws (i.e., acts of worship) is unsound; because although they are not addressed, ghusl is not obligatory due to janabah itself so that it could be said that at the time of obligation he was not addressed. Rather, its obligation is upon intending prayer and the like, and at that time he is a Muslim in a state of janabah. And if he embraced Islam and was not in janabah, ghusl is recommended for him due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever comes wanting Islam, if he is junub let him perform ghusl, otherwise not.' (Miskin and others)
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage opens by clarifying the ruling for a disbeliever who becomes Muslim: if he was in a state of janabah (major ritual impurity), ghusl becomes obligatory upon embracing Islam. The commentator then addresses an objection: some argue that since disbelievers are not addressed by the shari'ah (i.e., not obligated to perform acts of worship), their state of janabah before Islam should not necessitate ghusl after becoming Muslim. The Hanafi response is that ghusl is not made obligatory by the mere state of janabah; rather, it becomes obligatory when one intends to perform prayer or similar acts. At that time, the person is a Muslim in janabah, so the obligation attaches. If the convert was not in janabah, ghusl is recommended (mustahab) based on the hadith: 'Whoever comes wanting Islam, if he is junub let him perform ghusl, otherwise not.' This hadith directly supports the distinction. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is a standard Hanafi ruling found in the foundational texts.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, typically due to sexual intercourse or seminal emission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ghusl is recommended but not obligatory
B) Ghusl is obligatory
C) No ghusl is required because disbelievers are not addressed by the shari'ah
D) Ghusl is only required if he had performed no ghusl during his disbelief

Key Takeaway
The obligation of ghusl for a convert depends on whether they were in janabah at conversion; wajib if janabah, sunnah otherwise.
